Important News

Guerrilla Fighters Everywhere in Northeast China 91

Northeast Economy Completely Bankrupt

The Needs and Hopes of the Guerrilla Fighters

Another Derailed Train on the Anfeng Line

Japanese Slaughter Under Newly Agreed Articles

Correspondent from Peiping, visitor from Jilin talks about: (1) Since the September 18th Incident, the Northeast has been ravaged by the iron heels of Japanese bandits. Farmers cannot farm, merchants cannot trade, and the suffering of the people is beyond description. This year, rural crops have some hope for a good harvest due to favorable rainfall, but many areas along the South Manchurian Railway have been destroyed by Japanese invaders. Moreover, battles occur at any time and place due to the activities of guerrilla fighters. Wealthier villagers, whose economic conditions can be somewhat maintained, have moved to cities to seek refuge. Those who cannot afford it have joined the guerrilla fighters. Currently, it is feared that no one will harvest during the autumn harvest. Urban commerce is declining daily, and large and small stores are closing down one after another. The rural economy and the urban economy have been completely bankrupted by this sudden change. (2) Guerrilla fighters are everywhere, fleeting and unpredictable, constantly engaging the enemy in battle. Their resistance is quite strong, and the national spirit is being awakened. In the three northeastern provinces, apart from a few famous cities where large numbers of Japanese troops are stationed with sophisticated weapons and can barely maintain order, all other villages and towns are under the control of guerrilla fighters. The guerrilla fighters have no salaries, naturally suffering hardships. However, the people have a clear understanding of the guerrilla fighters and maintain close ties, so the guerrilla fighters have the potential for long-term resistance. (3) The people of the Northeast yearn for the Han Chinese more than ever. Two companies of Xi Qia's guards recently mutinied. A certain guard of five companies attacked Wang Dianchen's unit, but because they had no will to fight, Wang seized two howitzers and many rifles, and killed the reverse unit's company commander and deputy company commander. Wang was originally a bandit leader but has now engaged in national salvation work and has about fifteen hundred men. Also, the puppet troops in Changchun are unwilling to wear the [Manchukuo] badge. If they cannot avoid it, they treat it as a sign of being a conquered slave. The city is surrounded by guerrilla fighters, the situation is critical, and the people are panicking. (4) The people of the Northeast, grieving over the national crisis, have risen up in a national salvation movement. Based on observations, the guerrilla fighters have four advantages: (1) They endure hardship and are hardworking. (2) Their marksmanship is accurate. (3) They are familiar with the geography. (4) Their morale is high. However, due to long-term resistance, they urgently need two things: (1) Military and political talents. (2) Economic assistance. At the same time, they hope for two things: (1) That more domestic intellectuals will join the work. (2) That compatriots at home and abroad will provide economic assistance.

Visitor from Shenyang talks about: (1) At 11:00 PM on the 24th of this month, an express train departing from Busan derailed near Diaoyutai around 2:00 AM on the 25th because seven rail spikes had been removed by guerrilla fighters. The entire train derailed at that time and was fired upon. Captain Watanabe of the Japanese Independent Garrison was injured, and several people, including Ikeda, were killed. Seeing that the guerrilla fighters' activities were becoming increasingly fierce and trains were repeatedly derailing, the Japanese authorities have decided to stop some trains in advance. If the situation deteriorates further, they will stop all trains. The following trains are scheduled to be temporarily suspended: the first train between Ryongsan and Busan, the second train to Qiaotou, the sixth train to Benxihu, and the eighth train to Caohekou. As for the third and sixtieth light oil cars, they have been completely stopped. (2) Seeing that the activities of the guerrilla fighters are becoming increasingly serious, the Japanese authorities have forced the puppet state to promulgate two temporary laws for punishing traitors and bandits, purely as an excuse to prepare for the slaughter of our people in the Northeast. The law for punishing traitors has a total of sixteen articles, and the law for bandits has nine articles. The content is extremely cruel, unprecedented in the world. Anyone who violates them will be sentenced to death. The provisions of the two laws are too numerous to list in detail. (3) Since the green gauze tent (referring to the harvest season), the counties have received no revenue. Officials at all levels are showing signs of indolence because they have not received salaries for four months, especially in Faku County. Recently, the county's finance bureau has been unable to support itself due to the huge expenditure on security fees. (August 30th)

The Tragic Situation of the Harbin Flood 92

(Continuation)

The Puppet Authorities Had No Disaster Prevention Preparations From Beginning to End

Japanese Soldiers and Police Took the Opportunity to Oppress the Flood Victims

The Entire City Became a Watery Grave, Few Escaped

▲Puppet Officials Talk Empty Words – After the Ma Chuan Kou and Matsuura areas were flooded, people in Harbin thought that the floodwaters were discharged from that direction and that Jiangnan would be spared from danger. However, the floodwaters in Jiangnan did not abate slightly. On the 4th, the puppet Special Zone Administrative Chief Zhang Jinghui invited military, police, and legal entities to a meeting to discuss emergency rescue measures. The leaders of thirty-nine organizations and groups immediately decided to build a two-foot-high brick dam on top of the existing dikes and stack a five-foot-wide layer of sandbags. The funds were to be advanced by the Chamber of Commerce. On the one hand, they sent personnel to inspect the dikes along the Songhua River in Daoli Zhengyanghe at night to see if there were any dangers. If they felt that emergency rescue was necessary, they would also build brick dams and stack sandbags. Although this was passed by the entire meeting at that time, no one responsible supervised the work the next day (the 5th). On that day, the water rose another foot, and only one foot of the brick dam was exposed above the water surface. In the lower areas, there were only eight inches left. The puppet mayor, Bao Guancheng, who loudly advocated organizing a flood prevention committee, continued to do as he pleased and ordered private shipping companies and groups along the river to recruit laborers to block the flood in sections. As a result, they were secretly competing with the various organizations and groups invited by Zhang Jinghui, effectively meaning that neither party was responsible for flood prevention. On the afternoon of the 6th, the floodwaters rose even higher, and only seven inches of the brick dam remained. That night, they received a report from upstream, vaguely stating that a flash flood had erupted in Changbai Mountain, with waves as high as sixteen feet, and had reached Jilin. It would arrive in Harbin in three days. At this point, the merchants began to panic. The Chamber of Commerce also knew that Bao and Zhang were unreliable, so they gathered dozens of firefighters and workers to rush to protect the dike that night. However, the brick dam was thin, and that night it was breached in several places, with water pouring in. The foundation of the stone dam could not withstand the water's impact, and water seeped from under the foundation. By midnight, the floodwaters continued to rise unabated. Apart from the Chamber of Commerce and dozens of workers using old-fashioned methods of filling with soil as the water came, most of the responsible organizations and groups were asleep, with no one caring. At 4:30 AM on the 7th, the river broke through the dike, starting from Guiren in the twelfth district of Daowai.

▲Dike Breach – At 4:25 AM on the 7th, the floodwaters rose and the north wind blew strongly. When the stone dam in the eleventh and twelfth districts of Daowai was built in the past, the supervisor colluded with the contractor, skimping on materials. As a result, the stone materials were not pure, and the water was swept by the wind and temperature with great force. At 4:30 AM, it broke open from under the base of the dam, and the raging waves poured in. Immediately, about five zhang of the dike was destroyed. At that time, seven or eight workers hired by the Chamber of Commerce were standing on the top of the dam and did not have time to run away, resulting in them being swept into the water by the waves and washed away downstream in an instant. After the dike was breached, the fire department immediately sounded the alarm and rang the bell, awakening the citizens. On the one hand, someone suggested quickly going to the nearby flour mill to move flour and throw it into the breach. Chamber of Commerce officials did not make an immediate decision because the cost was relatively high. In the meantime, the floodwaters came like a mountain, and it was no longer possible to cope.

▲Chaos in the City – The water flowed from the eleventh and twelfth districts into the Binjiang North and South markets near the dam, which were originally formed by sediment from the Songhua River and were about a zhang lower than the river surface, so they were flooded first. Because the area east of Sixteenth Street was low-lying, the floodwaters flowed eastward first. In an instant, Twentieth Street was submerged in water. The floodwaters then gradually flowed west through Sixteenth Street. In less than three hours, four-fifths of Daowai was flooded. Around 10:00 AM, the water depth was thirteen to fourteen feet from Sixteenth Street to Twentieth Street, eight feet from Sixteenth Street west to Seventh Street east, and four to five feet from Seventh Street west to First Street east. All the buildings in the city were submerged in water. Most of the two-story buildings east of Sixteenth Street disappeared. The earthen and thatched buildings along the Binjiang River were not visible above the water surface at all. When the fire department sounded the alarm at the time of the dike breach, 200,000 merchants and residents in Daowai were awakened from their sleep. They scrambled to find vehicles and hire people to move their belongings. Zhengyang Street and Xincheng Street were plunged into chaos for a time. Vehicles and pedestrians were crowded along the way, and the cries of the old, the young, and women shook the sky. Traffic at all major intersections was blocked. At this time, the Japanese military police and the troops stationed in Harbin were fully armed and dispatched to guard the streets, prohibiting the flood victims from escaping to Daoli. They were forced to be exposed in the wilderness. Vehicles and horses were in a jumble, and those flood victims who forgot the traffic rules in their panic were beaten in the street. Those who wanted to return to move their belongings and rescue their families were not allowed. The price of vehicles and manpower soared dozens of times in an instant. Flood victims who could not find transportation or who felt sorry for their belongings ran to the roofs, without thinking of escaping. By the afternoon, the floodwaters continued to rise. Large sailboats could be sailed in the city. Merchants and residents who wanted to hire transportation to move their belongings and transport small items still could not easily do so. Even if they found transportation, it was intercepted by the puppet military police with guns to transport the belongings of the puppet chief officials' families. Japanese troops also seized many boats and roamed the city for fun, actually regarding the Chinese people's anxiety in the water or their crouching on the roofs as a source of laughter. Therefore, less than one-tenth of the 200,000 merchants and residents in the city escaped. As for the merchants' goods, none of them were able to move out. The amount of losses is incalculable. In the evening, the Japanese authorities sent additional members of the Retired Soldiers Association, holding weapons to assist the Japanese military and police in guarding the area, claiming to prevent counter-revolutionaries. They did not care about the Chinese people who were trapped in hunger and drowning. (To be continued)

▲Daoli Submerged – After Daowai was submerged, the residents of Daoli were still at ease. The puppet authorities also publicized that they had sent people to supervise the emergency repairs of the dangerous sections of the Zhengyang River dike. The general public still trusted them without doubt. At 11:00 PM on the 7th, the river broke through the Zhengyang River dike, and water poured into the Xin Zhengyang River residential area. Puppet Mayor Bao Guancheng began to show signs of panic. Puppet Administrative Chief Zhang Jinghui was senile and muddleheaded, and did not get the power he wanted, so he turned a blind eye to it. The Japanese authorities also deliberately stood by and watched, with the mentality that drowning all the Chinese people would facilitate the immigration policy. They knew that the water would flood Daoli, so they pretended not to hear and not to see. By the morning of the 8th, water had poured into the Thirty-six Shed, the East Railway Factory, and the Xinanbu area, all of which were flooded. It was only a li away from Daoli's prosperous streets. At this time, Bao Guancheng sent Section Chief Cheng Liuxian of the Public Works Section and Guo Chenggai to spend 100,000 yuan on emergency rescue, supervising the filling of sandbags at various street intersections separately. They organized it in a hurry, and there were no rush sacks to buy, and it was not easy to dig dry soil. Even Liu and Guo colluded to embezzle the money, so they only hired forty or fifty laborers to stack sandbags at the intersection of Xinanbu and Daoli and at the intersection of Thirty-six Shed and Daoli. They knew that the water had already entered the city and the flow was extremely easy. It was better not to block it. After blocking it, it increased the impact force. Therefore, as of noon, the north and south ends of Central Street in Daoli, and the Paotai Street, Gaoshi Street, and Xiewen Street were all turned into watery graves, with a depth of four to five feet in the deep areas and two to three feet in the shallow areas. For a time, residents and shops moved to Nangang, and the chaos was even worse than when Daowai was flooded. In the evening, the water depth in Central Street was four feet, and all traffic was cut off. At this time, the Japanese authorities gradually feared the accusations of consuls from various countries, so they dispatched all the members of the Retired Soldiers Association to assist the flood prevention committee of the puppet municipal bureau in carrying out flood prevention work. However, the disaster had already occurred, and it was difficult to effectively block it. Hirose Kotobuki, the commander of the 10th Division of the Japanese Army stationed in Harbin, was deeply afraid that the guerrillas lurking outside the city would take the opportunity to attack, so he instructed Zhang Jinghui to recommend him to take over the position of Japanese-Manchukuo Garrison Commander, issuing a notice on disaster relief and flood prevention. Bao Guancheng and Zhang Jinghui, according to the wishes of the Japanese authorities, canceled the flood prevention committee of the puppet municipal bureau and formed an emergency committee for the flood disaster. Zhang Jinghui was the president, Li Shaogeng, the director of the East Railway, and Komatsubara, a colonel in the Japanese Special Service Agency, were the vice presidents, Bao Guancheng was the chairman, and Yagi, an advisor to the Special Police Department, was the vice chairman. The committee had eleven internal divisions for planning, flood prevention, accounting, supervision, epidemic prevention, relief, procurement, transportation, propaganda, fundraising, and investigation. Various organizations and groups of the puppet state and Japanese organizations in Harbin sent people to join the work. Only then was there a relatively concrete organization, but the disaster had already occurred. More than 300,000 households of residents and merchants in Daoli were immersed in water.

▲The Tragic Situation of the Flood Victims – Since Daoli continued to be flooded on August 9th, Xincheng Street and Shuidou Street, which were located on high ground, as well as the areas where the Japanese lived, were also several feet deep in water. The entire area of Daoli, except for a few dozen zhang of Xincheng Street and Shuidou Street, was submerged in water. Because the shops had nowhere to move, and they were unable to hire boats for transportation, they built brick dams in front of their doors to prevent the water from rushing in, but the water flowed from the shadows.

Page 11

Important News 93

Water seeped into cellars, oozed from floorboards, and the indoors were still unavoidably flooded. Those with multi-story buildings took refuge on the second and third floors. Those without buildings either nailed their doors shut, leaving a few people to sit on the rooftops to watch over their property, while the majority of workers sought refuge in Nangang. In Daowai, for eight or nine straight days, the water level continued to rise, submerging the second and third floors of buildings entirely, and many houses collapsed. Well openings were also submerged, causing panic about drinking water. Those who had not been able to escape initially stayed on rooftops, and driven to extremes of hunger and thirst, disregarded the filth and drank the accumulated water from the streets. Obtaining fire was also difficult, so they could not cook food. All small boats had been commandeered by the authorities, and even paying a price of ten-odd dollars to be ferried out of the city was impossible. It was not until the eleventh that the Red Swastika Society, acting from charitable motives, repeatedly pleaded with the Japanese side to agree to seek and hire dozens of small boats to form a rescue team. They were dispatched to various streets to find and rescue disaster victims, transporting them to Nangang to live in the open. Because they were busy with the rescue, they were not allowed to carry miscellaneous belongings, so the disaster victims had to reluctantly abandon all their possessions and leave with only what they were wearing. The rescue was not completed until the fifteenth and sixteenth. There were still tens of thousands of people who were unwilling to abandon their belongings and remained steadfast in the water, making their own rafts to struggle against the floodwaters. At the same time, some people were also building rafts and boats, rushing into the water to retrieve miscellaneous items to survive. The floodwaters gradually encroached upon the border between Daoli and Daowai. Roads such as Xǔ Gōnglù, Jǐngyáng Street, and Zhōngmǎ Road were all submerged in a vast expanse of water, with depths of about three to four feet. It was not until after the eighteenth that the water level began to stabilize. In Daowai, only Táohuā Alley, Kùdāng Street, Rényì Alley, and Dà Shuǐjīng Street remained unflooded. After the twentieth, the entire city of Harbin, except for the residential areas near Nangang, Mǎjiāgōu, Xiangfang, Gùxiāngtūn, and Tiánjiā Distillery, was submerged. The commercial districts of Daoli, Daowai, the Eight Stations, and Xin’an Port were completely flooded. Since the twenty-first, the river water has not risen or fallen significantly. The water level on the twenty-third, measured at the main current, was 134.08 meters deep, which is more than 50 meters higher than usual. As for downstream areas, the flooding was also severe. Because the Songhua River does not flow directly into the sea, the discharge is very slow, and it is difficult to expect the water level to drop significantly in the short term.

▲ Food Panic 94

After the city was flooded, the prices of daily necessities and staple foods such as rice and flour skyrocketed immediately. Flour increased by five or six jiao per bag (30 jin), and rice increased by one yuan per bag (45 jin). Other items also increased in price by 100% or by one-third to two-thirds. Meat and vegetables were also unavailable, and initially there was nowhere to buy them. It was not until after the sixteenth and seventeenth that the puppet government, with permission from the Japanese side, allowed vendors to set up temporary straw sheds in unflooded areas of Nangang, Daoli, and Daowai to sell goods. As a result, straw sheds lined the streets in the unflooded areas, and stalls were densely packed. The puppet government also issued orders to crack down on price gouging, with the investigation department supervising investigations daily and punishing three or four merchants who raised prices excessively. As a result, prices dropped slightly, but were still more than double what they were before the flood. The stocks of rice and flour in the city were depleted due to a lack of sources or because they were flooded, so flour mills had not resumed production. Xiechangyong, the largest grain store, had approximately 300 shi of grain in storage, but because it was located by the river in Daowai, it was completely flooded, with losses estimated at three to four million. The stocks of grain in other grain stores were also not moved out in time. According to an investigation by the Flood Prevention Department, the total amount of food stored in Harbin was not enough for the city to consume for 20 days. Grain-producing areas along the river were all affected by flooding, and the wheat harvest was hopeless. In a month, the people will feel an extreme panic about food. Therefore, discerning people, after the Harbin-Changchun transportation was restored a few days ago, all moved south to avoid the disaster. The area affected by this flood is so large that there is no one responsible for providing relief afterward. The crisis is lurking, and the future is worrying.

▲ Great Fire in the Water 95

In Daowai, which was already flooded, a major fire broke out on August 9th. The fire started at Tianyitang Pharmacy on the east side of 11th Street. The water depth there was more than ten feet. The fire burned from inside the two-story building, starting at 6:00 AM and not being extinguished until 11:00 PM. More than 230 buildings in the vicinity were destroyed. Although the fire brigade witnessed the fire, the water was too deep for the fire trucks to drive to, so they allowed it to burn out on its own. However, when the fire was spreading, a suspect named Jia Kuiyi was arrested and taken to the Public Security Bureau for questioning. He confessed that he had a personal grudge against the landlord and took the opportunity to set the fire to vent his anger. He was placed in custody awaiting transfer to the court, but the suspect actually took advantage of the police's inattention and drowned himself in the water at night. On August 17th, another person named Yang Changshan also set fire to the Sun family's building on North 7th Street in Daowai to vent his anger. He was arrested by the police and beheaded in public on the 20th. Puppet police and Japanese military police have been patrolling in boats in shifts for days, and security has been tightened compared to before. Various agencies in Daowai have been moved to Nangang or to ships due to the flooding. Important military, police, and administrative agencies are continuing to operate as usual, while judicial offices and less important agencies have temporarily suspended work.

▲ Plague Rampant 96

In addition to those who have relatives and friends to turn to, nearly 70,000 disaster victims are living in the open in Nangang, divided into three areas east of Xu Highway. One area is along the upper embankment of Nangang, one is along Jile Temple Street, and one is along Shan Street to the Confucius Temple. In addition, the Puppet Government’s Extraordinary Flood Disaster Relief Committee borrowed land from various schools and public places to accommodate disaster victims, setting up a total of 23 shelters. Each shelter accommodates about 10,000 people at most and about 1,000 people at least. The total number of people living in shelters is approximately 80,000. Those living in the open in Nangang were initially exposed to the wind and rain. Before the 17th, there were several heavy rainfalls, and the disaster victims, especially women and children, cried out miserably, which was heartbreaking to witness. In the past week, the Extraordinary Flood Disaster Relief Committee has allocated funds to the Red Swastika Society to build straw sheds, one shed per household or one shed for every few households. Although this has fortunately prevented them from being exposed to the elements, they are still unable to shield themselves from heavy rain. Now that the weather is turning cold, disaster victims are contracting cholera due to being exposed to dampness, and hundreds of people are dying every day. The Japanese side, fearing that the plague would spread to their troops, specifically demanded 100,000 yuan from the puppet government to specifically handle disease prevention. Disease prevention injections are administered daily. However, the disease prevention team performs operations regardless of the strength of the Chinese people's bodies, forcing them to get vaccinations, causing many people who were not sick to become sick. The general disaster victims, fearing injections, run away by the thousands every day. As for food, the Red Swastika Society distributes 12 taels of large pancakes or four steamed buns per person per day. Because most of these are moldy and rotten, many disaster victims get sick after eating them. Disaster victims who had original jobs are trying to maintain their livelihoods by retrieving their belongings from the water and setting up shops in the straw sheds, making the Nangang disaster victim area colorful and diverse, with all kinds of businesses. Regarding the relief efforts for disaster victims, the puppet government plans to drive them back to their original homes inside the customs. Those who are willing to go will be transported free of charge by the South Manchuria Railway and the Chinese Eastern Railway. Those whose original homes are in the Northeast will be transported to Shuangcheng and Acheng counties for resettlement. However, many disaster victims are unwilling to leave immediately because their accumulated property is still in the water. They would rather endure their miserable lives and wait for the water to recede before cleaning things up. However, those who do not have much savings have agreed to leave Harbin, and their numbers are also very large. Recently, the Chinese Eastern Railway built a row of plank houses on high ground between the Xinzhengyang River and Xin'an Port, which can accommodate more than 10,000 disaster victims, and allocated dozens of train carriages to be parked near the 36th Shed to accommodate disaster victims. Foreign merchants from the United Kingdom, the United States, and other countries who reside in Harbin have also formed an International Relief Association and set up a shelter at the French University, which accommodates thousands of disaster victims.

▲ Flood Drainage Plans 97

The water level has not dropped significantly, and the city's originally low-lying areas are unlikely to drain into the river on their own. Therefore, the Puppet Government’s Extraordinary Flood Disaster Relief Committee plans to use drainage methods. However, pumping machines are difficult to find immediately, so they have specifically ordered ten units from foreign trading companies, each unit costing more than 20,000 yuan. Daoli and Daowai are divided into two zones, with Daoli and Xin'an Port as one zone, to carry out the first phase of drainage. Daowai is one zone and will be the second phase of drainage. The first phase is scheduled to install pumping machines on September 2nd and is expected to be completed by September 20th, but this depends on whether it does not rain in the coming days and the river water does not rise again. Daowai has too much accumulated water and is difficult to construct, so it must wait for the water level to drop slightly before draining it. It is expected to start in early October and take one and a half months to drain, completing the drainage by mid-November. Businessmen in Daowai are very dissatisfied with this plan because they feel that it prioritizes one area over the other. Moreover, Daowai is the commercial center, the water is deeper, there are more disaster victims, and the accumulated water has already begun to stink. Houses have been flooded and countless have collapsed. Flood prevention is disease prevention. Logically and morally, Daowai should be prioritized over Daoli. They have presented their reasons and strongly argued with the Extraordinary Flood Disaster Relief Committee, but the committee is controlled by the Japanese, so they insist on their plan. The Japanese side believes that Daoli is a foreign residential area and fears criticism from foreigners, so they prioritize Daoli, neglecting Daowai, where hundreds of thousands of Chinese people rely on for survival. However, various groups in Daowai still believe that if the Flood Disaster Relief Committee's plan is implemented, the accumulated water in Daowai will become increasingly smelly, and the spread of germs will be even faster. They fear that there will be no hope of draining the water before it freezes, and the property losses of the 200,000 residents of Daowai will not be less than 40 to 50 million. Therefore, they are spontaneously uniting and plan to imitate the Daoli plan, contracting drainage machinery to carry out pumping. According to general observations, Daowai's prosperity, regardless of the current situation of national subjugation, oppression, and economic decline, cannot be expected to recover in the short term. Even if there is a slight hope that the Northeast can be restored, it will not be possible for at least six or seven years. As for the accumulated water in the city, it currently has a pungent odor, making work extremely difficult. If it is delayed for one or two months, the turbidity of the water will be unimaginable. In recent days, anyone going to Daowai has been wearing sanitary masks, but they are still unable to block the pungent odor.

▲ Northern Border Crisis 98

Among the cities and towns along the river that have been most severely affected by flooding, in addition to Yilan, Tangwang River, Lianjiangkou, Xinchengzhen, Suibin County, Fujin County, and Jiamusi are also heavily impacted. Tangwang River and Lianjiangkou were completely submerged, and countless residents died. Fujin, Xinchengzhen, and Suibin County are all the richest grain-producing areas. After being flooded, the stored grain stones were all submerged. In the past, the staple foods and exported soybeans and wheat in the Northeast all came from these counties. Now, due to the flood, the people of the Northeast have no source of food. In addition to the cities and towns downstream that were flooded, the Chinese Eastern Railway line and the upper reaches of the Songhua River and the Nen River basin were also affected by flooding. The three lines of transportation of the Chinese Eastern Railway have long lost their flexibility. The Miaotaizi, Fularji, and Boketu areas on the Harbin-Manzhouli line were also heavily flooded, and traffic has been interrupted since late July. The Chinese Eastern Railway has allocated more than 250 material cars and summoned more than 5,000 workers to repair the roadbed, but it was still washed away by the water. After strenuous repairs, passenger and freight trains between Harbin and Ang'angxi were finally opened last week. The section from Ang'angxi to Manzhouli is still closed. Due to the heavy flooding of the Ashi River, the Harbin-Suihua line only allows passenger and freight trains to reach Ashihe Station. The area east of Ashihe is still closed. Caigou Station on the Harbin-Changchun line was flooded in late July, with the tracks flooded for 285 kilometers and the roadbed washed away. Traffic was cut off. Vehicles from Harbin only go to Shuangchengbu, and vehicles from Changchun go to Caigou Station. In the middle where there is water, small boats are used for communication. It was not until August 20th that a pontoon bridge was built, and passengers traveling back and forth had to get off the bus north and south of the bridge and walk 370 meters. The railway bureau measured that the tracks would be repaired on the 25th to achieve full line operation, but to this day (25th) there is still no confirmation of the opening of the line. The Japanese side said that the Soviet Union intends to block traffic, is not actively involved in restoring it, and intends to create chaos in northern Manchuria to facilitate the opportunity for communism. Although the statement is excessive, the Soviet Union definitely has this intention. At present, many barracks have been built outside Manzhouli, and international communist propaganda teams have been sent to the Dongning area to carry out propaganda. This is also worthy of attention. (August 25th)

Chiang Kai-shek's Measures in the Victory over the Communists 99

Relieving the People's Hardships and Preparing for Relief

Rectifying Military Discipline and Prohibiting Opium Smoking

A dispatch from Hankou states that Chiang Kai-shek, Commander-in-Chief of the Communist Suppression in the provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, has recently paid close attention to the relief of the people's hardships, the preparation of relief, the rectification of military discipline, and the prohibition of bad habits in the wake of the victory over the Communists. On August 31, he specifically issued measures to reduce and exempt land taxes in the counties affected by the Communists, urged evacuees to return to their homes, officially appointed county magistrates as military judges, and stipulated measures to prohibit opium smoking by party, government, military, and educational institutions. These are the most important measures in the victory over the Communists, and their details are recorded as follows:

▲ Reducing and Exempting Land Taxes in the Counties Affected by the Communists 100

Commander-in-Chief Chiang stated that the counties in the provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui that have been affected by the Communists have now been gradually recovered. To implement disaster relief and care for the people, in addition to already instructing subordinates to find ways to provide relief, he has also formulated temporary measures for reducing and exempting land taxes in the areas affected by the Communists. On August 31, he instructed the three provincial governments to follow the measures. The order stated: "In order to carry out the order, it is hereby stated that the red bandits are cruelly destructive by nature and indiscriminately burn and kill. In all areas that they have ravaged, most people have died, their homes have been reduced to ruins, and strong men have been displaced, and the fields are barren. As a result, even in years when the five grains are abundant, the people still have to worry about famine. Since I, the Commander-in-Chief, came to Hubei to supervise the suppression of the Communists, all areas affected by the Communists in the provinces have been gradually recovered. However, according to the reports from the military commanders, the various cruel and desolate situations are rarely seen in ancient history. In accordance with the principles of disaster relief and care for the people, we should urgently formulate a plan for recuperation and rehabilitation. Therefore, we have specifically formulated temporary measures for reducing and exempting land taxes in the areas affected by the Communists in the provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, and promulgated them for implementation to alleviate the people's hardships. After the order is implemented, all military and political leaders in the recovered Communist areas must strictly comply with it and strictly prohibit any attempt to levy taxes on any pretext or to deliberately impose harsh taxes. In addition to separate orders, we are issuing a copy of the temporary measures for reducing and exempting land taxes and ordering you to comply with them and instruct all counties in the Communist areas under your jurisdiction to comply with them as well. This is important."

▲ Urging Evacuees to Return to Their Homes 101

On August 1, Commander-in-Chief Chiang instructed the Hubei Provincial Government, the Pacification Committee for Communist Suppression of the Garrison Headquarters, and the Hubei Rural Reconstruction Promotion Association to encourage evacuees from all counties to return to their homes and assist in relief efforts. Those who do not return by September will have all of their original homes and properties distributed to disaster victims. The original order is as follows: "In order to issue an order, I, the Commander-in-Chief, lament the rampant spread of the red scourge and the suffering of the people. Since I came to Hubei to supervise the suppression of the Communists, thanks to the efforts of the officers and soldiers of the armies, the areas affected by the Communists in central and eastern Hubei have been gradually recovered. However, it has been repeatedly reported by the armies suppressing the Communists on the front lines that all the recovered counties have suffered because the local gentry have mostly evacuated and have not returned, so no one has come forward to take responsibility for all the relief efforts that need to be carried out locally. This has a great impact on the future of eliminating the remaining bandits and restoring local prosperity. The only way to remedy this situation is to quickly urge the gentry from all counties who have evacuated to return to their hometowns by a set date and jointly prepare for relief. I have recently made active and detailed plans for all the recovered counties, including local security, the recruitment of displaced persons, and the relief of the people's livelihood, and have sent cadres to the counties to conduct on-site inspections in order to implement them as quickly and effectively as possible. We rely on the concerted efforts of the people and gentry of the area, and the military and political leaders at all levels to cooperate sincerely and openly, so that all the important relief policies can be promoted to their fullest extent and the prosperity of peaceful and contented life can be restored as soon as possible. Otherwise, after the cruel burning, killing, and looting by the red bandits in the recovered areas, they will become a desolate and smokeless zone. Even if sages and philosophers are reborn, they will not be able to do anything on their own. In the past, when the Taiping Rebellion rose, its power was so great that it spread throughout the Yangtze River basin, which is far more powerful than the current red bandits. However, Zeng Guofan, Zuo Zongtang, Peng Yulin, and Li Hongzhang, whether they were gentry in their hometowns during periods of mourning or scholars who were well-versed in the classics, once they aroused their loyalty and righteousness, they relied on the efforts of three or two people to revitalize and advocate, and to maintain the declining fate of the Qing Dynasty. Therefore, it is known that the days of national crisis and danger are precisely when people of high ideals and benevolence should wear their official hats and let down their hair. Moreover, now that foreign enemies are encroaching and the national crisis is becoming increasingly urgent, if domestic pacification can be achieved quickly, we can naturally strengthen our prestige to resist foreign aggression. Gu Yanwu said that every man has a responsibility for the rise and fall of the world, and this is the time. For this reason, we order you to quickly investigate the gentry in the counties in the recovered Communist areas who have evacuated, to advise and urge them to return to their hometowns by the end of September, to make efforts for their local lives and families with a warm heart for saving their hometowns and saving the country. If they fail to return after the deadline, it means that they are willing to abandon the land of their ancestral tombs and only seek personal pleasure and comfort. All of their original homes and properties will no longer be taken care of by themselves, and they will be used to distribute to the local disaster victims to meet the needs of emergency relief. In addition to separate orders, we order you to comply with this order, advise the gentry in the recovered counties to return to their hometowns by a set date to prepare for relief matters, participate in the close organization of the people, strengthen the local self-defense forces, and be careful not to hesitate and delay, lest you regret losing your homes. We also order you to thoroughly investigate the names and addresses of the gentry in all counties in Hubei affected by the Communists (whether or not they have been recovered) who have evacuated to Wuhan and report them to the headquarters. This order is important." At the same time, it also ordered the Pacification Committee to supervise the gentry from Xianning traveling to the province to return to their counties by a set date (To be continued)

Local News

Songjiang 102

▲ Disturbance Among Prisoners in the County Prison 103

There are more than 100 prisoners in this county prison, many of whom are opium addicts. On the afternoon of the 28th, a disturbance suddenly broke out among the prisoners, who shouted in unison for food, reaching the outside of the prison. Warden Su immediately reported it to the county magistrate and requested the Public Security Bureau to send police to suppress the riot. After receiving the report, County Magistrate Shen, together with the president of the court and the prosecutor, entered the prison and gave the prisoners cordial advice, and the turmoil gradually subsided before they were locked up again. There are various theories about the cause of the disturbance among the prisoners. Some say that the amount of food distributed to the prisoners did not match the prescribed weight, which seems credible. The next day, the warden investigated the ringleaders and mistakenly identified a prisoner named Yang, an opium addict who was about to complete his sentence, as the instigator and brought him out for punishment. He was severely beaten on the buttocks with rattan whips, with bloodstains and numerous scars, which was unbearable to witness.

▲ Education Bureau Holds Teacher Registration 104

The provincial government believes that elementary education is very important, and in order to select teachers, it previously held examinations and certifications. Now, this county's education bureau has received an order from the provincial government to hold elementary school teacher registration, issue regulations, and send letters to the education committees of each district, who will forward them to the teachers of each school to fill out forms and submit them. The location of the future examinations in this county is designated at Shanghai Provincial High School. There are six requirements for this year's registration. All teachers from normal schools and secondary schools under the old system must submit verification certificates, photos, and other documents.

Suzhou 105

▲ Will Jiangsu Province Implement Public Opium Sales? 106

The rumor of public opium sales has gradually become a reality. Yesterday, Feng Hechá, a commissioner from the Hubei Special Tax Office stationed in Jiangsu Province, came to Suzhou from Zhenjiang to meet with County Magistrate Zou at the county government to discuss everything and request assistance. According to Mr. Weng, a member of Feng's entourage, he has been ordered to come to Suzhou to discuss the public sale of special tax goods. The stamps for these special tax goods are all affixed in Hankou and transported to Suzhou. After arriving in Zhenjiang, they are transferred to various counties. The locations for the public sale of special tax goods in each county have already been determined by the province, with each county having four or five to more than ten locations. The procedure requires special tax merchants in each county to register with the province first, and only after obtaining approval can they receive special tax goods for sale; otherwise, they will be treated as selling privately. The Jiangsu office is located in Zhenjiang, and there is also a general office located in Hubei. No branch offices are established in each county, nor is any kind of name or signboard used. The public sale period for these special tax goods is limited to three months, and it will be stopped as soon as the province's finances are slightly eased. Yesterday, more than a dozen people in Suzhou who wanted to buy and sell these special tax goods contacted Commissioner Feng to discuss the procedures. Once everything is settled, it can be realized.

Taicang 107

▲ Zhu Tieying Goes on a Hunger Strike in Prison 108

Zhu Tieying, the editor of the Taicang Moxie Daily, was arrested for writing about business tax matters, stating the difficulties of businessmen and appealing to the director of the business tax bureau. Unexpectedly, he angered the county government. On the afternoon of August 29, at 3:00 PM, Zhou Wenqing, a special agent from the county government, led police officers to summon Zhu Tieying to the county government for questioning. Zhu immediately followed them to the county government, where County Magistrate Zhao personally interrogated him and accused him of inciting businessmen and resisting the payment of national taxes, fining him 100 yuan and sentencing him to one year in prison. The next morning, the newspaper was banned from publication and the newspaper office was closed. As a result, Zhu Tieying was imprisoned and tasted the flavor of iron bars. Currently, all sectors of Taicang are greatly angered because the counties affected by the war have been exempted from all taxes after discussions by the provincial government. Now, County Magistrate Zhao has accused Zhu of attempting to overthrow the national government and harming the interests of the Republic of China for appealing to the people, and everyone is greatly angered and has risen up to support him. It has also been heard that Lu Jingshi, Zhu Shuren, Hu Yanggang, Dai Yongchan, and others from the same township living in Shanghai are particularly agitated and are determined to rescue Zhu from prison. Because he has been unjustly imprisoned, Zhu has been on a hunger strike since the day before yesterday to urge the authorities to wake up.

▲ New Merchant Steamboat Robbed En Route 113

The Wuyi New Merchant Steamboat Changsha班 set sail from Changzhou on the 29th at about 9:00 PM. Four or five people who looked like workers were found on the boat. At this time, the "workers" inside the boat also came out and forced the captain to approach the shore. Before long, the bandits swarmed onto the boat and looted at will. The captain and passengers lost a great deal of silver dollars, valuables, and jewelry. In addition, there have been a series of robberies in Wuyi in recent days. Wuxi 115

▲ Arrest of Thieves Cutting and Stealing Electric Wires The Qishuyan Power Plant's office in Wuxi, for the sake of electrical convenience with the Qishuyan Power Plant, had hung two pairs of No. 12 wires on existing utility poles. This allowed communication between Wuxi and Qishuyan, commonly known as "intercom lines." Unexpectedly, in July, a section of this intercom line behind Xiyuan in Huishan was suddenly cut and stolen, rendering it unusable. After re-hanging the wires, the lines were restored to their original state. However, in August, a section of the same line was cut and stolen three times in succession. The Wuxi Electrical Affairs Department instructed Wu Jinrong, a line patrol worker, to investigate covertly. Simultaneously, three telephone wires at Wangxueyan Bridge in Wuxi were also cut and stolen south of Wuqiao. At that time, Wu Zhihui, an important figure in the Party, was unable to call the city due to the incident. He immediately instructed Yao Dixing, the head of the county's Construction Bureau, to investigate and reconnect the lines. Director Yao, upon receiving the order, instructed Li Jingqing, another line patrol worker, to investigate and report. On August 19th, Wu Jinrong and Li Jingqing, working together at Xin Sanli Bridge in Beitang, apprehended a thief named Li Jugen, along with a coil of No. 12 copper wire. They were handed over to the Fifth Branch of the Public Security Bureau and then transferred to the County Public Security Bureau. They were then sent to the County Court, where Prosecutor Shen held a hearing and immediately ordered their detention. Yesterday, the workers Wu Jinrong, Li Jingqing, and police officer Shi Jie were summoned to court to testify. After their testimony, they were immediately indicted and transferred to the trial court. However, the power plant and the Construction Bureau believed that Li Jugen's cutting and stealing of the electric wires was not an isolated incident and could not be treated as a simple theft case. They insisted that he be punished under the crime of endangering public transportation. Therefore, they have separately sent letters to the County Court, requesting that he be severely punished.

▲ Bao Ying Sends Police to Escort Captured Bandit Leader At Wangjia Bridge, on the border of Gaoyou and Bao Ying, a large number of bandits had entrenched themselves a few days ago. Zhu Hua, the captain of the county's police force, upon receiving the report, immediately led his team to cooperate with the Bao Ying Self-Defense Corps in suppressing the bandits. They killed one bandit, Ding San, on the spot and captured the bandit leader, Hu Ba, and a suspected accomplice, Zhang Xiaocaizi. Captain Zhu immediately escorted Hu and Zhang to the city and transferred them to the county government for legal proceedings. After interrogation, Zhang Xiaocaizi was released on bail, while Hu Ba was shackled and imprisoned. Because Hu had committed numerous crimes in Bao Ying, the county government has now specifically sent an official letter to Gaoyou, requesting that Hu be brought back to Bao Ying for legal action.

Jiaxing 117

▲ Resolution of the Qixiu School Land Occupation Case Since the abolition of warehouses in Xicangji, north of Jiaxing, You Xiuliang had negotiated with the authorities to rebuild the Qixiu Girls' School (a private school founded by the You family). However, the area was vast, totaling over 29 mu, and had been occupied by the You family for over a decade. This time, due to the demolition in the northern city, a local citizen, Wang Liangchen, reported the matter to the authorities. However, the You family, oblivious to the situation, claimed that the warehouse land was ancestral property and requested a court trial. Ultimately, due to a lack of evidence, the case remained unresolved after more than two years of litigation. Subsequently, the educational authorities discovered that You had issued a land borrowing agreement when the school was rebuilt. They then reported to the province for instructions. The province recognized the land as public property and ordered the county to assess its value and collect taxes. The six mu already registered under Qixiu's name should also be thoroughly investigated to determine if the land tax payment was legal at the time. It is now known that the county government, upon receiving the order, has assessed the 23.25 mu of land occupied by You at a price of 500 yuan per mu, referencing the neighboring commercial school's old site. You is required to pay 11,625 yuan. The land occupation case, unresolved for several years, can now be considered concluded.

Important News 120

Ministry of Education Emphasizes Military Education 121

Nanjing, 1st - The Ministry of Education, noting that a significant number of high schools and above in various provinces and cities have not yet implemented military education and that military instructors should be dispatched to carry out training, has ordered all specialized schools and above that have not yet implemented military education to submit accurate reports of their student numbers, class numbers, and grade numbers within one month of receiving this document to facilitate overall assessment and allocation.

Nanjing, 1st - The Ministry of Education issued a circular to the education departments of various provinces and cities, stating that the purpose of school academic affairs meetings is to improve the overall academic affairs of the school. Military education is one of the academic subjects, and all military instructors should attend and participate in these meetings to facilitate timely consultation and improvement. This is to be relayed to all public and private high schools and above under their jurisdiction for compliance.

Ministry of Education Orders Universalization of Rural Public Education in Various Counties 122

Nanjing, 1st - The Ministry of Education issued a circular to the education departments of various provinces and cities, stating that, according to the report submitted by the China Social Education Society, past social education efforts have tended to focus on cities and neglect rural areas. Future improvements should focus on rural public education. To this end, Gao Yang, a member of the society, has drafted a plan for the universalization of rural public education in various counties of Jiangsu Province, which has been adopted and implemented by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education. Jiangning, Wuxi, and Nanhui counties have been tentatively designated as pilot areas, and other provinces may follow suit. Therefore, the original draft plan is being forwarded and presented, requesting that various provinces and cities designate several counties for pilot implementation. Considering that our country is currently facing unprecedented national difficulties, and to truly awaken the national consciousness and self-rescue spirit of the people, it is imperative to vigorously promote the universalization of rural public education. The various sections of the original draft plan are essential and can serve as a reference for various provinces and cities to promote public education. A booklet of the plan is being printed and issued for reference in pilot implementation.

Ministry of Education Clarifies That Vocational Schools Can Establish Film Departments 123

The Ministry of Education, based on a report submitted by the China Vocational Education Society, notes that the Shanghai Women's High School stated in a letter that film is a powerful tool for modern education, and that all European, American, and Japanese countries actively promote it, with universities establishing specialized departments and normal schools often including it as a required course. Elementary schools often use film as an aid to teaching. In addition, institutions such as the National Educational Film Review Office of Germany, the National Educational Film Review Office and Film Education Academy of Italy, and the Film Education Research Association of the Japanese Ministry of Education, and the National Children's Film Museum of Soviet Russia all serve as important evidence of the importance of film education. Although there have been enthusiastic advocates in our country in recent years, there is a lack of corresponding facilities. The school, recognizing this, plans to add a film education department in the next semester to cultivate specialized talents. However, due to the pioneering nature of this endeavor, there is a lack of clear standards in terms of the educational system. Furthermore, it involves vocational education, and a special letter is being sent to your society for interpretation or to request instructions from the Ministry. After reviewing the film project, it is indeed a powerful tool for modern education and should be guided and specialized talent cultivated to meet the needs. However, the level of education required and the type of school to which it is equivalent have not been specified in our country's educational system. Therefore the Ministry is requesting instructions. The Ministry of Education clarified that while film can indeed be a powerful tool for modern education, it currently has no standing in the existing educational system. With the exception of vocational schools, girls' high schools and other formal schools may not establish film departments or specialized classes. This is for your information and dissemination.

Teng Gu Earns Doctorate in Art History 127

Teng Gu, a former professor of art history at the Shanghai Art College, went to Europe in 1929 to study art history. He was recently approved by the Prussian Ministry of Education to take his degree examination. After being interviewed in turn by the heads of philosophy, art history, archeology, history, and other departments, he passed each one and was formally awarded a doctorate. The overall comment was the Latin word "Egregie." The degree examination in art history and archeology at the University of Berlin is very rigorous. Scholars from other countries spend five or six years at the very least, or more than ten years, still waiting to be selected. Dr. Teng, however, obtained the degree with two or three years of effort. Moreover, Dr. Teng is the first Chinese person to obtain this degree, which is a supreme honor internationally. It is reported that Dr. Teng is scheduled to return to China from Germany this month and will continue to teach at the Shanghai Art College.

Liu Shi, a young painter and nephew of Liu Haisu, has been dedicated to the arts since childhood. His works are outstanding and have long been renowned among his peers. His solo exhibition, featuring his past works for the public, is being held from yesterday to the 10th at the China Arts and Crafts Society, 45 Rue du Père Froc, Avenue Amééie Cognacq, in the French Concession. The exhibition includes over 180 pieces, all vibrant and lifelike. His recent works from Putuo (26 pieces) and relics from the Shanghai War (20 pieces) are particularly rare masterpieces. It is reported that many domestic celebrities, such as Lin Sen, Li Shizeng, Cai Yuanpei, Jiang Menglin, Chu Minyi, and Chen Gongbo, have provided sincere introductions and inscriptions of praise for Liu's solo exhibition. Unfortunately, the preparation time was very short. The exhibits fill five large rooms and are breathtaking.

Sports 138

The National Sports Conference Committee Revises the National Physical Education Plan 139

Nanjing, 1st - The National Sports Conference held its 14th committee meeting at 4:00 PM on the 1st to discuss the concluding matters after the conference. Chu Minyi chaired the meeting. 1. A motion was made to subsidize the Lizhi Society with 250 yuan. If souvenirs are needed, the funds will be transferred accordingly. 2. A motion was made to handle the closing procedures, including the implementation of the association's income and expenditure accounts, the implementation plan, the conference report, the conference material preparation committee's records, and the conference minutes. A letter will be sent to the Ministry of Education reporting the preparation and progress of the conference, letters of thanks will be sent to the experts who attended the conference, and letters will be sent to the organizations that sent representatives, sending them various items. 3. A motion was made to print 1,000 copies of the report. 4. The introduction to the National Physical Education Implementation Plan, section 5, and the implementation and promotion group's review report on teacher training, were revised. The revised plan is as follows: Introduction, 5. (The Position of National Arts in Physical Education) National Arts is the inherent physical activity of the Chinese nation. On the one hand, it can provide self-defense skills, and on the other hand, it can be used as a tool for physical exercise. It not only has its fixed value in national history, but also cannot be ignored from the perspective of modern sciences such as anatomy and physiology. The promotion of non-research is indeed an important goal today. Domestic physical educators should have a thorough understanding of modern physical education and its basic disciplines, and should not be self-deprecating or stuck in the past. This is indeed the necessary path to promote national arts. Implementation and Promotion Group, Teacher Training First Proposal: A motion was made to establish a national specialized school. It was resolved to incorporate it into the National Physical Education Specialized School or Physical Education Academy. Before the establishment of a specialized school, the National Arts Hall should be responsible for the training of National Arts teachers.

The 20th Army Defeats Youyou in Basketball Game Last Night 141

43 to 37

Tennis Team to Play Youyou This Afternoon

The basketball team of the Sichuan 20th Army Expeditionary Force demonstrated its strength for the second time last night, defeating the Youyou Sports Association 43 to 37 at the Youyou Basketball Court. The details are as follows:

▲ The 20th Army Leads from Beginning to End - A Smooth Victory The 20th Army led from the beginning to the end. In the first quarter, they defeated the enemy 16 to 9. The result of the first half was 31 to 18. After the change of sides in the second half, Youyou bravely counterattacked and once created a tense situation, gradually closing the gap. At the end of the third quarter, the score was 34 to 31, only a difference of three points. However, the 20th Army scored several times with excellent coordination, and the final score was 43 to 37.

Impressive Skills - The basketball skills of the Sichuan Army are probably the best among all ball games. The coordination is excellent. Several successful shots were the result of their skilled and rapid passing. It is a pity that they lack control in shooting and missed many opportunities. It is also not the best strategy to shoot from a distance and not dribble under the basket. The courage to fight is a characteristic of soldiers, but sometimes both sides are too aggressive, which is a minor flaw. The referee was Shao Leping. The scores of the two teams are recorded below.

City Government Issues Announcement Yesterday 146

Both Chinese and Foreign Authorities Have Spoken to Dispel Rumors

The City's Morale Was Slightly Calmer Yesterday

Due to rampant rumors in the city in recent days, the residents were quite apprehensive. After the Chinese and Japanese authorities issued separate statements clarifying that there would be no second war, people's morale began to stabilize slightly. Therefore, the number of residents moving out of the Hongkou and Zhabei areas decreased yesterday. Both Chinese and foreign authorities made statements yesterday to stabilize public sentiment. The compilation of these statements is as follows:

▲City Government Announcement: The Shanghai Municipal Government issued an announcement yesterday, stating, "For the purpose of public announcement, since the January 28th Incident, the people of this city, motivated by patriotic fervor, have eagerly sought to save the nation and society. Their righteous indignation has often manifested in radical actions. However, patriotic movements should strictly adhere to the boundaries of the law to avoid disrupting social stability and providing excuses for others. Otherwise, patriotism can easily mislead the nation, and saving the people can easily harm them. Recently, there have been frequent cases of threatening letters, even throwing bombs and injuring people in the Special District under the name of 'Blood Oath to Eliminate Traitors' or other names, disrupting public security and undermining order. This is extremely serious. The Mayor, in order to maintain local security, has repeatedly ordered crackdowns. If anyone still disregards the safety of the nation and society, they will be punished according to the law. It is hoped that all citizens will understand this and strictly abide by it without fail. This announcement is critical."

▲Yu Hongjun's Statement: Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun said to visitors yesterday, "Recently, rumors have been rampant. The general public does not carefully distinguish them and are easily alarmed, especially in the Nanshi, Zhabei, and western Shanghai areas. It is not surprising that citizens are afraid after the war. However, believing unfounded rumors and moving away en masse is not only unnecessarily alarming but also causes both mental and financial losses that are difficult to calculate. The City Government, to stabilize public sentiment and maintain public security, has issued an announcement yesterday, strictly ordering citizens to adhere to the boundaries of the law and not provide excuses for others. I firmly believe that the rumors circulating outside about a second war breaking out in Shanghai are merely speculations and not credible."

▲Cuninghame's Statement: Yesterday, Joint Committee Chairman Cuninghame stated to visitors, "The Joint Committee was established based on the Sino-Japanese Armistice Agreement of May 5th. Its mission of monitoring troop withdrawals and taking over has been completed. As for the recent rumors of Japanese troops setting up military telephones in western Shanghai and Japanese troops conducting armed demonstrations in the Hongkou area, I have not heard of them. Furthermore, the Sino-Japanese Armistice Agreement is still fresh, and there should be no further incidents. If, unfortunately, the situation in Shanghai becomes serious again, the Joint Committee can convene a meeting of the Joint Committee according to regulations upon the request of either China or Japan. As for whether the authorities of the Public Concession will allow the Japanese side to conduct military operations within the Concession again, I cannot answer on their behalf." Cuninghame also said that although the situation in Shanghai appears serious, much of it is rumor. He hopes that the Chinese and foreign press will be extra cautious in their reports to avoid further disputes.

Mayor Wu's Letter to the Citizens of Shanghai 147

Peace and Order are the Conditions for Shanghai's Revival and Development

Hope Citizens Recognize the Path to National Salvation and Avoid Frivolity and Impatience

I Pledge to Strive for Peace and Revival with Utmost Determination

Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng published a letter to the citizens yesterday, stating, "Shanghai is the economic center of our country and the hub of international trade. Its prosperity, governance, and chaos are not only related to the rise and fall of our national fortune but also to the interests of foreign nationals. Since the January 28th Incident, the overall situation has been devastated, vitality has been greatly lost, citizens have been displaced, and commerce has been depressed. Now that the war has ended, there are many scars waiting to be healed. All of my fellow citizens should be enduring hardship, working together to build up and revive, and pooling our wisdom and efforts to seek revival. When I, the Mayor, was appointed by the Party and the State, it was at a time when the Shanghai Incident was at its most tense. I did my best to overcome difficulties. Fortunately, with the loyal courage of the soldiers on the front lines defending themselves and the enthusiastic support of the people everywhere, we were able to restore peace to Shanghai. For the past six months, I have been thinking day and night, deeply feeling that after the serious damage to this city and the displacement of the citizens, it is imperative to recuperate and rejuvenate in order to seek revival. The only and most important condition is a foundation of peace and a state of order. Only peace and order can restore the vitality of this city, promote the development of this city, relieve the suffering of the citizens, and quietly seek a plan for the overall construction of this city in the future and remove all obstacles to revival and development. After extensive visits and consultations, and after quiet observation, I deeply feel that the citizens of Shanghai and the people of the whole country have suffered deeply and have reached the limit. I cannot bear to see them being subjected to unnecessary disturbances, further unnecessary disputes, and further unexpected devastation. I pledge to ensure the peace and order of Shanghai in the future with the greatest confidence, the greatest determination, and the greatest courage. All of my fellow citizens should also recognize the conditions for the revival and development of this city in the future, move your hearts, endure your nature, do not be angry at the spur of the moment, do not engage in superficial tensions, and do not engage in frivolous and reckless actions. You must know that the life of the nation is in grave danger, and a dying tree cannot withstand further felling. Last year, the Central Government announced to the people of the whole country that 'saving the nation and resisting aggression is the most difficult and serious task in the world.' What we should dedicate ourselves to our motherland is not a momentary impulse, not a momentary indignation, but a determination to fight permanently and strive to save the nation. The biggest weakness of mass movements in recent years is that they mistakenly believe superficiality to be reality and means to be ends. Therefore, they often abandon the fundamentals and pursue the superficial, recklessly use their efforts, and fail to accomplish anything and even ruin things. This is truly an undeniable weakness in the psychology of our people and the crux of the failure of national movements over the years. This is the sharp edge of why China's national morale is strong on the outside but weak on the inside, and why China's diplomacy has failed repeatedly. I, the Mayor, am determined to save the nation and am responsible for protecting the people. All of my fellow citizens should also consider the overall situation, love the nation, do not be frivolous, do not be impatient, do not overstep the bounds, and do not violate the law. Let patriotism be based on sincerity, and actions must be legal. Since the national crisis, labor unrest has been rampant, and the suffering from mutual attacks is even worse than before. Social instability and production stagnation have followed the war. How can the nation's lifeline and the people's lives bear it? At the same time, lawless elements are also borrowing names, overstepping the boundaries of their actions, inciting people's hearts and disturbing public security. If this continues, what hope is there? To secure the interior and resist foreign aggression, to save the nation and seek strength, is the duty of the Mayor. For such lawless elements who overstep the bounds, I will definitely deal with them strictly according to the law in order to maintain law and order and strengthen the foundation of the country. I deeply hope that patriotic compatriots and foreign residents in Shanghai will understand this and maintain the peace and order of this city, and strengthen the revival and development of Shanghai. I, the Mayor, have high hopes for this."

Ministry of Railways Explains Responsibility for Transportation 149

The Miscellaneous Grain and Oil Cake Association Proposed Seven Points

The Ministry of Railways Replied with Detailed Explanations of Each Item

Adding a 10% Fee is a Precedent Set by the Former Ministry of Communications

All Nineteen Items in the General Rules are Based on Civil Law

The Shanghai Miscellaneous Grain and Oil Cake Trade Association recently sent a letter to the Ministry of Railways, pointing out various shortcomings in the regulations for responsible transportation and requested instructions from the Ministry. It is now heard that the Ministry of Railways has replied to the Association with detailed explanations of each item. The general content is as follows: (1) Responsible transportation has long been practiced in various countries. Railroad transportation in our country has not been responsible, resulting in countless malpractices, which is undeniable. Merchants and people suffer from multiple layers of exploitation when transporting goods, which is extremely difficult (the average freight paid is 40% to 100% more than the railroad freight). The Ministry resolutely reformed this system to relieve the suffering of merchants and people. All equipment and procedures are adapted to responsible transportation. In order to unify the handling of affairs, it is inconvenient to implement responsible and non-responsible transportation at the same time, as this would result in the same malpractices and divergent handling of affairs. Moreover, railroad transportation should be responsible in principle. All railroads across the country will change from non-responsible to responsible, so there is no reason to keep both systems coexisting; (2) The reason for adding a 10% surcharge for responsible transportation is that there are records of general rules promulgated by the Ministry of Communications before the tenth year of the Republic, and this is not an exceptional addition. In the past, freight rates were calculated based on the transportation costs at that time. Now that responsible transportation is implemented, costs have increased significantly, such as adding freight yards, warehouses, tarpaulins, employees, road police, and compensation for losses. The meager 10% surcharge may not be enough to offset these costs. The multiple layers of exploitation suffered by merchants in non-responsible transportation are definitely more than this 10%. The actual freight expenditure is reduced rather than increased. As mentioned earlier, it is more than 40% to 100%. If only 10% is added, a lot of suffering has been relieved in the transportation aspect; (3) The priority loading method is precisely to eliminate the malpractice of privately selling train cars. The method is to start shipping in the order of arrival of goods at the station. However, it is bound to be inconvenient for goods with price or contractual special relationships, so we must find a way out for them. This regulation is purely for the benefit of the merchants; (4) Regarding the regulations for various expenses, the thirteen types listed in the letter are not all uniformly collected in reality. However, a very small number of fees are charged only when special equipment or procedures are necessary. According to past practice, the same fees must be charged when such facts occur, but this time it is less than before. For example, the ticket exchange fee used to be five yuan, but now it is called a change fee and only costs one yuan, which is clear evidence. Furthermore, not all of the listed fees must be charged item by item. Ordinary goods do not necessarily require fees other than freight, such as warming fees and refrigeration fees. Currently, there is no such equipment on various lines, so naturally, they will not be charged. Even if there is warming car and refrigerated car equipment on various lines in the future, the fees will still be limited to special fresh goods, and the purpose is still to facilitate merchants. (The original text explains and proves each item separately below, proving that fees are not charged item by item and that the fees are less than before. Because the original text is too long, it is not recorded here); (5) Goods arriving at the station at night are not calculated according to working hours, because the twelve hours from 6:00 p.m. to 6:00 a.m. the next morning are not working hours. Therefore, the twelve-hour work unloading restriction is actually equal to eighteen hours, which can be said to be sufficient. If this is not restricted, there will be too much inventory, blocking the station, which will inevitably hinder passengers and cargo. There is obviously a misunderstanding in the letter about this; (6) The issue of liability for railroad transportation is relatively non-absolute, limited non-unlimited, both in reason and law, as it is in all countries with no exceptions. The nineteen items in Article 36 of the Responsible Transportation General Rules, which the railway cannot be responsible for, are the same as the written regulations of railroads in various countries and can be reviewed. Railroads cannot be held responsible for force majeure natural disasters, changes in the nature of the goods themselves, or the fault of the cargo owner. The nineteen items in the general rules are based on the principles stipulated in the Civil Law and serve as the basis for the law. According to the principles, not only railroads can apply, but also transfer companies can apply uniformly; (7) Under the non-responsible transportation system, merchants suffer too much from layer after layer of exploitation. Now that responsible transportation is implemented, merchants can directly report the shipment, so transfer companies cannot hoard goods. The burden on merchants is reduced, so they should come back. There is no reason to turn to water transportation instead. Moreover, now that the above items have been explained, everything should be clear. We should have a deep understanding of the Ministry of Railway's plight in alleviating the suffering of merchants and people and developing the social economy.

Newly Appointed Japanese Military Attaché to Shanghai Issues Important Statement 150

According to the Japanese newspaper Shanghai Japanese Daily, the newly appointed military attaché candidate at the Japanese Consulate General, Colonel Yoshiwo Iwamatsu, arrived in Shanghai on the Nagasaki Maru from Qingdao on the 31st of last month and immediately stayed at the Towa Yoko. Iwamatsu served as the military attaché in Shanghai from 1926 to 1928, and was later transferred to Hiroshima and Taiwan. He is now being transferred to Shanghai again. He made the following statement to Japanese reporters: "This time coming to Shanghai is originally my long-cherished wish. Since leaving school, about two-thirds of my handling of Chinese affairs has been completed. Recently, it is the period of overall resolution of Japan's China problem. All the mistakes of the past China policy must be resolutely eliminated and properly handled. In addition to discussing with local knowledgeable people, I ask for the support of everyone to make the greatest determination."
