Ninghai Warship Held Flag-Raising Ceremony Yesterday 154

Captain Gao Xianshen Takes Office

Chen Jiliang Sent by the Ministry to Witness the Oath

The Ninghai warship of the Navy held a flag-raising and formation ceremony yesterday morning. At the same time, the ship's captain was sworn into office. The Ministry of the Navy will send Chen Jiliang, Vice Minister of the Ministry and Commander of the First Fleet, to represent and witness the oath.

▲A Glimpse of the Ceremony Platform The ceremony platform was under the flagpole at the stern of the ship, covered with red silk. The Party and national flags and the late premier's portrait were hung above. The captain's oath was on the left of the platform, and the military band platform was on the right.

▲Attendees Those who attended the ceremony yesterday included Chen Jiliang, Political Vice Minister of the Navy and witness, Chen Hongtai, captain of the Yixian warship, Luo Zhitong, captain of the Zhongshan warship, Sa Shijun, captain of the Chutai warship, Zeng Kouying, captain of the Chuqian warship, Zheng Gongyao, captain of the Minquan warship, Liu Defu, captain of the Ganlu warship, Wang Zhaoyuan, captain of the Puan warship, Chen Zaofan, deputy director of the Shipyard, Ye Baoqi, commander of the guard battalion, and dozens of representatives from the naval hospital and naval ordnance depot.

▲Ceremony Program (1) Assembly on deck; (2) Flag-raising at 8:00 a.m., with music played at the same time, the whole audience stands in respect and raises their hands to salute the national flag; (3) Witness and captain and guests take their places; (4) National anthem played; (5) Party song sung; (6) The whole audience bows three times to the Party and national flag; (7) The witness respectfully reads the late premier's will; (8) The witness presents the seal; (9) The captain takes the oath of office; (10) The witness delivers a training speech; (11) Guests deliver speeches; (12) The captain gives a response; (13) Slogans shouted: 1. Long live the Republic of China, 2. Long live the Chinese Kuomintang, 3. Long live the Navy, 4. Long live the Ninghai warship; (14) Ceremony complete; (15) Photograph.

▲Flag-Raising Situation At 7:50 a.m., all personnel, witnesses, and guest representatives gathered on the deck of the ship. At 8:00 a.m., the soldiers slowly raised the national flag. At the same time, the ships parked there also raised their flags amidst the sounds of national music and applause. After about two minutes, the national flag was flying in the sky.

▲Captain's Oath After the flag-raising ceremony, the captain's inauguration ceremony was held. First, the witness presented the seal. After the captain received the seal, he raised his right hand and respectfully read the oath, saying, "I respectfully swear that I will abide by the late premier's will, practice the Three Principles of the People, obey the orders of my superiors, defend the country, love the people, and fulfill the duties of a soldier. If I violate this oath, I am willing to be subject to the most severe punishment. This is my oath."

▲Chen's Training Speech After the oath, Chen Jiliang, the witness, delivered a training speech on behalf of the Ministry of the Navy, saying, "I, Jiliang, am honored to be ordered today to participate in the Ninghai warship captain's inauguration oath and flag-raising ceremony. I am pleased that at this time when the national finances are extremely difficult, it is not easy to complete this warship. This warship is quite powerful, but it requires the joint efforts of all officers and soldiers on the ship to be successful. I hope that all officers and soldiers on the ship will live up to the people's money and the purpose of the Ministry of the Navy."

▲Captain's Response After Chen's speech, Li Shijia, the chief supervisor, reported on the construction of the warship, followed by Captain Gao Xianshen's response, saying, "The Ninghai warship is the newest and largest, so I am deeply concerned that my talent is meager and my knowledge is shallow and that I will not be able to fulfill my duties. I hope that my colleagues will work together, obey the orders of our superiors, and fulfill our duties in order to live up to the people's expectations."

▲Jiang's Naming The name of the warship, Ninghai, was named by Jiang Zhongzheng, the former Chairman of the National Government. The text reads, "How beautiful is Ninghai, beginning a fine name, surging waves, bright light shining on the water, five teeth gleaming, three wings soaring, tracks around the islet, dispersing invading spears, banners shining together, bugles and drums sounding in unison, a dragon dreams of auspiciousness, forever celebrating a clear environment, undersigned by Chiang Chung-cheng, Chairman of the National Government.

▲All Officers and Soldiers of the Warship The warship has a full complement of officers and soldiers, including Captain Gao Xianshen, Lieutenant Commander Wang Zhiguang, Lieutenant Commander Lin Huiping, Lieutenant Commander Xue Jiasheng, Lieutenant Junior Grade Guo Hongji, Lieutenant Junior Grade Zeng Guoqi, Lieutenant Junior Grade Yu Weixin, Electro-Officer Xu Yu, Supply Officer Zhang Tianhong, etc., for a total of 42 officers, 31 sergeants, 250 soldiers, and 36 servants, totaling 361 people. They are scheduled to go to Nanjing at the end of this month.

The Bureaus of Finance, Social Affairs, and Land Took Over Gaoqiao and Fahua Districts Yesterday 159

The reason is that the scope is too small

Zhong Renjie, the municipal commissioner of Gaoqiao District, and Yang Hongjun, the municipal commissioner of Fahua District, submitted reports to the Municipal Government some days ago requesting their resignations. Mayor Wu ordered the municipal offices of Gaoqiao and Fahua districts to be abolished, and the local businesses handled by each district were transferred to the Bureau of Finance, the Bureau of Social Affairs, and the Bureau of Land, which separately sent personnel to Gaoqiao and Fahua yesterday (September 1st) to be responsible for checking and taking over the various inventories and reporting them to the Municipal Government.

City Government Revokes Two City Committees, Causing Repercussions 160

French Concession Citizens Plead to Retain Yang Hongjun

Gaoqiao Residents Request Reversal of Order

▲ Citizens of the French Concession, including Wang Xiangxun, submitted a formal petition to the City Government yesterday, appealing for the reversal of the decision to abolish the district's City Committee office. The following is an excerpt: "Petition for the Reversal of the Abolition of the City Committee Office in This District, Awaiting Consideration. We, the citizens, read in the August 25th newspaper a news item stating that your government's municipal meeting resolved to abolish the City Committee offices in Gaoqiao, the French Concession, and the Western District, which caused great consternation. This district is located in a strategic area, with a population of tens of thousands. Local administration cannot be suspended even for a day. Therefore, there was first the establishment of the township office, followed by the City Committee office. How could your government suddenly announce the abolition of the City Committee office in this district? We are truly perplexed. Furthermore, at the beginning of the City Government's establishment, the authorities, valuing local municipal affairs and accepting the public will of the district, appointed Mr. Yang Hongjun as the Municipal Affairs Commissioner for this district. Since Mr. Yang took office, he has been diligent and striving. In just a few years, the municipal affairs of this district have been completely renewed. The citizens are deeply grateful for having the right person in charge of the municipal affairs of this district. Once he departs, the future of municipal affairs in this district will be seriously affected. We, the citizens, who have grown up in this land, have a more direct understanding and cannot remain silent. Therefore, we specifically submit this document to appeal to your Excellency for review and approval, allowing the reversal of the abolition of the City Committee office in this district, and continuing to appoint Mr. Yang Hongjun as the Municipal Affairs Commissioner for this district, to comply with public opinion and value the local area. We await your urgent orders with utmost respect. Presented by the Citizens to Mayor Wu."

▲ The Municipal Affairs Commissioner's Office in Gaoqiao District, Pudong, had Commissioner Zhong Renjie resign due to personal matters. The City Government suddenly abolished the office. Local figures believed that during this transitional period, without a local organization to liaise, official-civilian communication would inevitably be hindered. Therefore, silk merchants and others from the district prepared a letter to the Pudong Native Place Association, unanimously seeking assistance and requesting the City Government to reverse the abolition order. The original letter stated: "Respected Sirs, the Municipal Affairs Commissioner's Office in Gaoqiao District has been abruptly abolished by order of the City Government due to the resignation of Commissioner Zhong Renjie, a personal matter. Not only will local administration lack a channel for communication, but even your association will have no one to consult regarding matters of common interest and the promotion of association affairs. Currently, the level of public knowledge is still rudimentary. Although the regulations of various bureaus and offices of the City Government are detailed and the proclamations are extremely courteous, the boundaries are distinct, and the public still finds it difficult to understand. Any requests or instructions lack a local liaison organization, leading to groping around, which will inevitably result in separation between officials and the people, and difficulties for both. Local politics will become unthinkable. We have long admired your association for prioritizing the welfare of fellow villagers and taking the promotion of hometown affairs as its primary task. We respectfully request that you promptly forward this to the Shanghai City Government, stating that the municipal organization in Gaoqiao District must not be fundamentally abolished due to the resignation of an individual. Please continue to establish it to achieve effective coordination. The members feel deeply concerned and cannot remain silent. We fear that directly presenting this petition might result in it being shelved without action. Therefore, we specifically appeal to your association for your assistance. The local area will be extremely fortunate."

Export Volume Report of Jiangzhe Old Factory Silk 162

According to the report from the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau's Raw Silk Inspection Department, from June to August 30th of this year, the export volume of old factory silk from Jiangsu and Zhejiang was 5,786 bales. 51% was shipped to France, 30% was sold to the United States, 13% was shipped to the United Kingdom, and the remainder was sold to Africa and India.

Flour Millers Request Anhui to Waive Passport Fees for Wheat 163

In July of this year, the Anhui Rice and Grain Inspection Office was reorganized into the Rice and Grain Administration Bureau. For wheat leaving the province by train, truck, or sailboat, a passport fee of 4 jiao and 5 li per shi was charged. When Jiangsu flour millers transport wheat from Anhui, the bureau also wants to collect the same passport fee. However, the millers argue that the "Regulations on the Announcement of Special Wheat Flour Tax by the Government in the 17th Year of the Republic of China" clearly stipulates the abolition of wheat li and the collection of flour tax, and that all taxes and levies similar to li on wheat should be abolished. The Anhui Province's collection of wheat passport fees, charging per shi and setting up checkpoints, is effectively a disguised form of li. Unwilling to pay, they, through the Jiangsu-Zhejiang-Anhui Inland Flour Millers Association, submitted appeals to the Ministry of Finance, the Tax Department, and the Taxation Administration, requesting a telegram to the Anhui Provincial Department of Finance, instructing the Rice and Grain Administration Bureau to cease collecting wheat passport fees and to immediately release the Datong Factory's wheat ship that had been detained. The relevant departments, well aware of the millers' suffering, have taken action accordingly. It is reported that the passport fees collected by Anhui Province are used for road construction. While the financial difficulties of the province are unavoidable, flour millers bear the burden of flour tax, and their business is already extremely difficult. Moreover, the badlands of Jiangsu and Anhui provinces are adjacent. Dasheng Pass is only a dozen kilometers away from Sanwen River in Nanjing. Once Jiangsu millers' wheat leaves Anhui Province, the cost increases by 4 jiao and 5 li per shi. The cost of flour is too disparate, and the future of the business is unthinkable. Yesterday, the Shanghai Flour Millers Association and the Jiangsu-Zhejiang-Anhui Inland Flour Millers Association held special meetings on this matter. They unanimously advocated appealing for the cessation of the collection. It is reported that the two associations received instructions from the Ministry of Finance, and have telegraphed the Anhui Provincial Department of Finance to cease the collection of wheat passport fees and release the Datong wheat ship. The Anhui Provincial Department of Finance has already replied to the Ministry that it will comply. Thus, the flour millers have reached a stage of resolution in the matter of waiving wheat passport fees.

Minutes of the Standing Committee Meeting of the Jiangsu Rice Association 164

The Jiangsu Ning-Shanghai County Rice Industry Association Federation held its tenth executive and supervisory standing committee meeting yesterday at Cuixiutang. The committee members present were Zhang Jingzhai, Zhao Zixin, Lu Zhuqing, Lu Gongquan, Chen Junyu, Zhu Zixiang, Yan Xiaoquan, Zhang Nianxuan, and fifteen others. Zhao Zixin was elected as chairman. After performing the formalities, the meeting discussed the proposal from the Wuxi, Suzhou, Changshu, and other trade associations that the Jiangsu Provincial Government promulgated regulations to increase business tax, distinguishing between rice and miscellaneous grains and classifying them for additional taxation. The association members pointed out that those engaged in the business of miscellaneous grains mostly also sell rice, and there has never been any distinction. Moreover, food grains are related to people's livelihoods, and it is unacceptable to increase the burden. The motion to unanimously strive to avoid distinction and additional taxation was passed. A petition was submitted to the Jiangsu Provincial Government, appealing for the continued collection according to previous practices, to maintain the people's livelihood. Furthermore, the Wujiang County Rice Industry Association proposed that rice prices are falling daily, and the rural economy is on the verge of bankruptcy. They requested that the association submit a petition to the Executive Yuan, appealing for permission to circulate rice grains in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, to alleviate rural distress. The motion was passed, and a petition was immediately submitted to the Executive Yuan, requesting instructions to the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial governments to issue orders for circulation. Lu Gongquan temporarily proposed that the autumn harvest of this year is about to take place, and rice and grain production and income survey forms should be issued for investigation. The motion was passed, and the association immediately printed and distributed the forms to its members for completion and return. In addition, Committee Member Zhu Zixiang handed over a letter from Committee Member Zhao Zixin, with an attached petition from Hu Jia and others. Because the letter seemed different from Zhao's previous letters, he was asked to personally identify it. Zhao declared that the letter was not from him, and he did not know about the attachments. He said that he would strictly investigate who was playing this trick. The meeting decided that since Zhao denied the letter, the petition from Hu Jia and others should not be discussed. The letter and petition were retained by the association.

Baoshan Public Groups Oppose the Collection of Land Tax for Road Construction for the Province 165

Yesterday, a Joint Telegram was Sent to the County Government

Requesting the Provincial Government to Withdraw the Order

The Baoshan County Public Funds and Property Management Office, Education Bureau, Poor Children's Education and Welfare Center, and various district chiefs telegraphed the county government yesterday, stating: "We recently received an order from the provincial government that, starting from the 21st year of the Republic of China, half of the land tax collected for road construction in each county should be remitted as provincial funds, and that the county should report the remittance on a monthly basis. We are extremely shocked. Since the establishment of the Transportation Bureau (renamed the Office after the establishment of the Construction Bureau) in Baoshan County in the spring of the 11th year of the Republic of China, loans have been taken out for road construction. Over 10 years have passed, and more than 100 li of east-west and north-south county roads have been completed. However, over 70,000 yuan in public and private debts remain outstanding and have not been repaid. The Chengyue Road project was temporarily suspended due to the war and urgently needs to raise funds for construction. If half of the land tax is remitted to the province, the debt and construction projects will be seriously affected. This is the first reason for requesting exemption from remittance. Furthermore, when the city and county regions were divided in the 17th year of the Republic of China, due to debts and unfinished county roads and bridges, there were various related relationships. After discussions by representatives from the Ministry, the provincial government, and the city government, it was decided that the Transportation Office would continue to exist. The land tax for road construction within the city area would still be collected by the Shanghai City Government and allocated to the office for use. This was approved by the National Government upon submission from the Ministry of Interior. Currently, the land tax for road construction within the city area is still allocated to the county for use according to the original plan. However, the county area is now required to remit half of its funds to the province. This is not only unfair, but also risks affecting the agreements between the city and county. This is the second reason for requesting exemption from remittance. Moreover, the provincial and county expenses should be clearly divided and should not be mixed. If this precedent is set, the county funds will lose their guarantee, and county projects will be more difficult to carry out. Furthermore, the county has just suffered from war, with deep wounds and severe pain. Roads and bridges that were destroyed are being repaired, and funds are especially needed. This situation is unique. This is the third reason for requesting exemption from remittance. Therefore, we urgently telegraph and beseech the County Magistrate to review and submit this to the provincial government, to approve the reversal of the order, to maintain the debt and prioritize county construction projects. We await your orders with utmost respect."

Reasons for Delaying the Repair of the Tanjiabang Embankment 166

Cheng Ouchu's Letter to Tang Chengzong

Mu Ouchu's Letter to Tang Chengzong stated: "Respected Sir, I received your telegraph yesterday, which stated: 'Recently, strong winds and tides have been raging. The embankments along the Wusong River, where the Japanese army bombarded, have collapsed. The Tanjiabang area is also collapsing daily. If a large autumn tide occurs, a major disaster is inevitable. The committee member has witnessed the current situation and is deeply concerned. Therefore, he urgently informs you, hoping that you will quickly implement the original plan and proceed as soon as possible to prevent any eventuality.' Furthermore, I read in the newspaper that you had issued news stating that a resolution had been reached, but it has not been implemented. After the Shanghai Incident, economic panic ensued, and funds were depleted, making fundraising impossible. Therefore, we had to work within the scope of the 810,000 yuan that could be raised, to address the most urgent projects. All the schemes have been examined and approved by the engineering experts and were submitted to the meeting for public deliberation. Upon detailed examination of the records, the Wusong Tanjiabang project was not within the scope of the projects funded by existing funds. Furthermore, out of caution, I personally went with Committee Member Zhang Xiaoliang and Committee Member Shen Xuansun to inspect the site. We concluded that although the Tanjiabang seawall was thin, it was high. Although the water flow was winding, it was not eroding. If there is no extreme headwind, there will be no danger. And compared with other sections, it is closest to Shanghai, with convenient transportation. In case of emergency, materials for emergency repairs can be delivered immediately. Therefore, we addressed the most urgent issues and could not take everything into consideration. However, I am constantly mindful of it. It is just that my strength is insufficient, and I only feel ashamed. Fortunately, you are also a member of the seawall committee and attend every meeting, so you must be aware of all the difficulties. Moreover, I would like to inform you that after the autumn floods of this year, there have been repeated storms. I am well aware of the importance of the seawalls in each section. Due to insufficient funds, repairs could not be carried out. There are many places like Tanjiabang. In case of an accident, I would have no way to face the local people and no way to face my conscience. Therefore, in addition to the post-disaster reconstruction projects, I raised tens of thousands of yuan separately and prepared materials such as wood and stone for emergency repairs. It is like using troops, where I have to draw a mobile force from the thin defense force. Now, the local area is blessed, and there have been no major errors in August. However, there is still a risk of an accident before September 18th. I am trembling with fear and unable to sleep peacefully. I respectfully ask you to consider that we are in the same boat, inspect the area at any time, and send a telegram immediately if there is a warning, so that I can supervise the emergency repairs. I would be deeply grateful. Respectfully, I wish you good health. Mu Xiangyue."

China's Coal Mines 168

China's coal reserves are abundant, but the mining industry has been slow to develop. Transportation difficulties often lead to wasted resources, while foreign coal floods the market. In Shanghai, for example, most of the coal used in the past was Japanese, resulting in a significant outflow of profits, which is lamentable. Recently, fueled by patriotic fervor, Chinese people have gradually begun to promote domestically produced coal, which is welcomed by the nation. It is also essential for the country to understand the overall assessed volume, as coal is a vital national mineral resource. Therefore, we are publishing this special investigation so that the people will recognize that the land is not stingy with its treasures and will work together to exploit them to their fullest potential. If they do, the achievements in the future will be remarkable. Let us offer our best wishes.

According to a survey by the Geological Survey Institute, Shanxi province has the most coal reserves, followed by Hunan, Sichuan, Yunnan, and Guizhou. Next are Hebei, Henan, Shandong, Jiangxi, and Gansu, and finally, Jiangsu, Anhui, Zhejiang, and other provinces. The following is a report of the quantities:

(In thousands of tons) (In thousands of tons)

Shanxi 5,830,000 Shaanxi 1,000,000

Hunan 1,600,000 Anhui 205,000

Sichuan 1,500,000 Zhejiang 120,000

Yunnan 1,200,000 Fujian 150,000

Guizhou 1,300,000 Guangxi 500,000

Hebei 2,270,000 Guangdong 300,000

Henan 1,755,000 Jiangsu 190,000

Shandong 685,000 Jiangxi 85,000

Gansu 1,000,000 Hubei 130,000

Rehe 930,000 Suiyuan 460,000

Chahar …… Heilongjiang 160,000

Jilin 160,000 Fengtian 985,000

According to the above table, China has 23,435,000,000 tons. Dr. Drake's statistics estimate 996,612,700,000 tons, while Mr. Inoue of Japan estimates 39,973,000,000 tons. Although the numbers vary widely, it is clear that the reserves are abundant.

As for the mining industry, from the Guangxu era to the present, over the past forty years, there are still only a few dozen companies in the country organized in various provinces using new methods for mining. These include the Jiawang Company in Jiangsu, the Lieshan and Guan Kuang Bureau in Anhui, the Naizishan Company in Jilin, the Yudong and Muling Coal Mine Companies, the Changxing Company in Zhejiang, the Ludong and Zhongxing Companies in Shandong, the Hegang Coal Mine and Zhalannuoer Coal Mine Company in Heilongjiang, the Baojin Company in Shanxi, the Kai Feng and Jingxing Zhengfeng Companies in Hebei, the Fushun, Yantai, Benxi, Huwu, Huzui, Xi'an, and Badaohao Coal Mine Companies in Liaoning, the Beipiao Company in Rehe, the Fu Company, Zhongyuan and Liuhegou Companies in Henan, the Lincheng, Yili, Zhonghe, Zaitang, Liujiang, Mentougou, and Jimingshan Coal Mine Companies in Hebei, and the Pingxiang Company in Jiangxi. The rest are all small, traditional kilns, which operate intermittently. Even these existing dozens of companies are either facing economic difficulties or are being reorganized due to incidents. In summary, it can be said with certainty that most are still far from achieving development.

The situation of mining and operations in various provinces varies and is difficult to describe in detail. Shanxi province has the highest output in the country, so we will briefly describe Shanxi province as an example of the general situation.

Shanxi province is located on a plateau, surrounded by mountains, with an area of 549,200 square miles. Except for a dozen counties in the southern Hedong Circuit that have no coal, more than 80 counties have coal. According to a survey by the Geological Society, Shanxi has 2,370,000,000 tons of anthracite and 3,460,000,000 tons of bituminous coal. The counties with the most coal are Cheng, Changzhi, Huguan, Changzi, Gaoping, Lingchuan, Jincheng, Yangcheng, Qingshui, and Yicheng, which have 1,100,000,000 tons of anthracite and 210,000,000 tons of bituminous coal. Shouyang, Mengxian, Pinding, and Xiyang counties have 1,000,000,000 tons of anthracite. Datong, Zuoyun, and Huairen counties have 1,000,000,000 tons of bituminous coal. It can be said that there is almost no place in Shanxi without coal.

Shanxi produces about 2.1 million tons of coal per year, only 36/10,000 of the total coal reserves in the province. As for its testing results, the anthracite produced in Heshun County contains 0.58% moisture, 16.41% volatile matter, 28.89% ash, 54.70% fixed carbon, and 8430 calories. The coal produced in the Wencheng area contains 0.9% moisture, 18.7% volatile matter, 20.0% ash, 61.3% fixed carbon, and 7350 calories. The coal seams may either appear on the surface or have many layers. The deepest seam in Pingyao County has 12 layers, each about four feet thick. The thickest seam is up to seven feet thick. The sequence of layers is as follows: first yellow sand, then gray-blue sandy rock, then two inches of coal, then shale and white sandstone, then one inch of coal, then shale, then one foot of coal, then sandstone, then one foot of coal, then shale, then two feet of coal, then sandstone, then one foot of coal, then white sandstone, then four feet of coal, then white sandstone, then four feet of coal, then white sandstone, then one foot eight inches of coal, then shale, then three feet of coal, then shale sandstone, then four feet of coal, then sandstone, then seven feet of coal, then sandstone, then four feet of coal, and finally gray-blue stone rock. The tested composition and calorific value can reach 5678 calories. The Datong area in Shanxi Province has the most coal. Among the local companies, Baojin is the largest and has the most mining sites. The mining area in Heilongwumiao, Shigangzhuang Village, etc., covers 27 square miles and 90 acres. The mining area in Wuguantun, Jiangjiawan, etc., covers 47 square miles. Both new and traditional methods are used. The Jin Hua Company's mining area in Yungang, Shitoucun, Xiaoyutongcun, etc., covers 44 square miles and nine acres. The annual output is 40,000 tons of coal. The Guangxing Company's mining area in Gangou covers two square miles, uses traditional methods, and also produces 30,000 tons per year. The Tongshi Company's mining area in Changliushui Village covers more than 5,000 acres and produces 40,000 to 50,000 tons per year. The Yujin Company's mining area in Datong covers more than 5,000 acres and produces 150 tons per day. The Baofeng Company's mining area in Xiaomafengjian also produces 30,000 tons per year. In addition, there are more than 60 smaller companies, mostly using traditional methods, with annual outputs ranging from more than 10,000 tons to 4,000 to 5,000 tons, and the least producing 500 to 600 tons.

Furthermore, the coal mines in Northeast China are also very rich. Our country still lacks accurate statistics, but the Japanese have been paying attention for a long time and are doing their best to investigate. According to statistics, the three northeastern provinces produce 1,317,000 tons of iron, 9,250,000 tons of coal, 400 to 500 tons of lead, 700 to 800 tons of copper, more than 20,000 tons of magnesite, and 23,000 tons of talc annually. The unexploited coal reserves, according to Japanese surveys, are 4,209,760,000 tons. The current annual coal consumption in the three provinces is only 2.5 million tons, which is enough for more than 1,680 years. The following is a list of the locations and reserves:

Location Reserves Coal Quality

(In ten thousand tons)

Fushun 1,000,000 tons Lignite, bituminous coal

Xingan District 120,000 tons Lignite

Hewu Gang 1,500,000 tons Bituminous coal

Jiulantun 220,000 tons Lignite

Muling Mishan 1,000,000 tons Bituminous coal

Dongning 98,000 tons Bituminous coal

Central North Manchuria Lignite Layer 31,760 tons Lignite

Central Jurassic Fire Layer 200,000 tons Bituminous coal

Lafa River Coalfield 50,000 tons Lignite

Other locations 80,000 tons

Total 4,209,760 ten thousand tons

Given China's abundant coal reserves and limited mining, the demand for coal increases every year. Taking Shanghai, the largest coal-consuming market in China, as an example, the consumption was 1 million tons in 1918, increased to 2 million tons in 1924, and 3 million tons in 1929, and has continued to increase to this day. However, imports from outside the customs in 1928 were 2,432,932 tons, 2,281,230 tons in 1929, 2,467,042 tons in 1930, and 1,902,890 tons in 1931. In terms of value, it is more than 20 million taels of customs silver each year, with Japan being the largest contributor. In addition, there are imports from Annam, England, Hong Kong, and other countries. The extent of the outflow is clear. Those who are concerned about the times, with the fervor of advocating domestic goods, should take this important and major coal industry issue to heart and be even more vigilant.

Telephone Company Should Be Responsible for Line Disconnections 170

The Guowen News Agency reports that the Shanghai Special District Telephone Users' Association yesterday sent letters to the Shanghai Telephone Company and the Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association in the Shanghai Settlements, opposing the increase in telephone charges and the arbitrary disconnection of telephone lines. The two letters are recorded below:

▲ Letter to the Telephone Company: We are writing to inform you that your company, under the pretext of replacing new equipment, secretly requested the approval of the Public Works Department to increase charges and to retroactively calculate them from three months ago. The city's users are in an uproar upon hearing this. Telephones are a public utility. You cannot rely on monopolistic rights to seek one-sided benefits. You should consider the interests and burdens of the public. The price increase is one-third for quarterly fees and one-half for per-call fees. At a time when commerce is depressed and the market is weak after the war, efforts are being made to reduce the rental prices of houses needed for people's lives, and the Public Works Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council is also considering exempting the general rate on which municipal construction depends. Why is your company increasing prices at this time and retroactively to three months before the fiercest fighting? This not only violates the principles of social economics but also breaks the established precedent that laws are not retroactive. If this can be tolerated, what cannot be tolerated? Our association is organized by the city's users and is the only representative body for users. After repeated deliberations, we unanimously deny the increase and insist on paying according to the original prices before the case is properly resolved to help your company's turnover. This approach is fair. In addition to having requested the Ratepayers' Association to negotiate on our behalf, we are sending this letter to you in the hope that you will quickly cancel the agreed price increase and charge according to the old prices. We also hope that you will not abuse your power and arbitrarily cut off telephone lines to maintain the spirit of a public utility. Otherwise, it will incite other incidents, and your company should bear the corresponding responsibility.

▲ Letter to the Ratepayers' Association: (Omitted above) Recently, our association has repeatedly received reports from users that the telephone company is refusing to accept old prices and forcibly cutting lines. This situation is enough to expose the company's reliance on the superior rights of a monopolistic business and its abuse of power. According to current laws, the relationship between creditor and debtor must go through mediation or trial by the court to determine the responsibility. The installation of a telephone is the same in nature as renting a house. The recovery of unpaid rent must go through legal procedures. Non-payment of telephone bills is at most a debtor-creditor relationship. How can the line be cut off directly, thereby preventing others from using it? This is very obvious (Omitted in the middle) How can the company force people to follow its arbitrary actions because it is not satisfied with its desires? Our association believes that the company's line-cutting is fundamentally illegal and is likely to cause other disputes and is not a way to resolve the price increase. We ask your association to quickly send a letter to the Public Works Department, strictly ordering the company to stop this illegal action. Otherwise, the company should bear full responsibility for any other unfortunate events that may arise. We are sending this letter for your information and consideration.

Tailor Cruelly Shackles Apprentice with Iron Chains 171

Apprentice Escapes at Night After Breaking Chains

Dai Jiabin Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment

Dai Jiabin, the owner of the Daishunxing Tailor Shop at No. 38 Juqing Lane, Xin Zha Road, and a native of Taixing, Jiangbei, needed an apprentice. His brother brought 14-year-old Huang Xiaolin from his hometown on the fifth day of last month to apprentice to Jiabin. He was left at the shop to learn the trade, but his treatment was exceptionally cruel, with severe reprimands at every turn. Huang, unable to bear the suffering, began to long for home. Jiabin preemptively, on the evening of the 30th of last month, used a very thick iron chain to suspend Huang from the beam, and used a thinner iron chain to tie his left foot and lock it, believing that he could rest easy and that it would be difficult to escape. Huang initially had no power to resist and had to submit to the arrangement. When everyone in the shop was sound asleep, he managed to break the joint of the thick and thin iron chains. Once freed, he did not hesitate, pushed the door open, and fled. When he reached Avenue Joffre in the French Concession, Patrolman No. 474 of the French Concession Police noticed him, finding it strange that he was holding a section of iron chain and that his left knee was also surrounded by an iron chain. He immediately took the boy to the French Concession Police Station and, after clarifying the situation, notified the Xin Zha Police Station the next morning. Detective Zong Weiting was dispatched to bring Huang, along with the evidence, back and arrested Dai Jiabin at the tailor shop for questioning. He then sent the child to Renji Hospital, where a doctor examined him, confirmed that there were several injuries, and filled out an injury report. Yesterday morning, they were sent together to the First Special District Local Court, where Judge Wu Tingqi conducted the trial. First, the police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated that the defendant was charged with the crime of obstructing freedom under Article 309 and the crime of injury under Article 293, Paragraph 1, and described in detail the defendant's cruel and brutal treatment of the apprentice and the process of solving the case. He concluded that the defendant's actions toward his subordinates were reminiscent of the unenlightened masters of the past. In the modern era, such self-centered treatment of subordinates has long been eliminated. Even if students do not listen to instructions, they should be guided and persuaded with kindness. To resort to beatings is a great betrayal of humanitarianism. He requested that the defendant be punished as a warning to others. Huang Xiaolin then stated that he had come to Shanghai with the defendant's brother on the fourth day of the seventh lunar month to learn the trade. His parents were still at home. The defendant would often beat him with a ruler for doing things poorly. Now he said that I wanted to return to my hometown, so he locked me with chains. When questioned, the defendant Dai Jiabin stated that Huang came to the shop to learn the trade with a contract for three and a half years. He had been in the shop for nearly a month, and he did not obey his commands, so he reprimanded him. The night before, he had secretly escaped and was sent back by a friend who found him on Datong Road. Because he was afraid that he would escape again, he used iron chains to lock him up. Judge Wu examined the statements and found that the defendant's treatment of the apprentice was indeed excessively cruel. He immediately sentenced him to three months of imprisonment for the crime of injury and five months of imprisonment for the crime of illegal detention, to be served concurrently for a total of six months. Huang Xiaolin will remain in custody until his family is notified to take him away.

Fujian Provincial Salvation Association's Telegram to the Central Government 172

Discussing the Standards for Reorganizing the Provincial Government's Personnel

The United Association of Fujian Native Organizations in Shanghai convened an emergency meeting to discuss the standards for selecting personnel for the upcoming reorganization of the Fujian Provincial Government. A unanimous resolution was reached to urgently telegraph the Central Government, requesting it to adopt the suggestions outlined in the association's previous petition to the Central Government. The original telegram is recorded as follows: To Chairman Lin of the National Government, Premier Wang of the Executive Yuan, and Acting Premier Song of the Executive Yuan: Fujian Province is unfortunate to have suffered from banditry. Fortunately, the Central Government has compassion for the people and has urgently dispatched a large army, which has greatly pleased the people of Fujian. However, for years, the province has been governed by the wrong people, leading to political corruption, oppressive taxes, widespread banditry, and popular discontent. If we want the suppression of the communists to be swift and successful, and the aftermath to be handled properly, we must simultaneously reform the government and thoroughly reorganize the provincial government to save the people of Fujian from their misery. Our association has previously collected the opinions of the people of Fujian on political reform and sent representatives to Nanjing to present them to the Central Government. We are now telegraphing the standards that our association believes should be applied in the selection of personnel for the provincial government, as follows: (1) The Fujian Provincial Government should be thoroughly reorganized. The selection of the chairman should be based on seniority, prestige, familiarity with the overall situation of the province, rich political experience and ability, and the ability to take responsibility. Anyone who has served as a member of the provincial government in the past with no political achievements or who has bad habits should not be selected. (2) The selection of provincial committee members must draw on talent from throughout the province and must not be monopolized by one faction or a small group of people, leading to a disconnect from popular sentiment and a deformed political system. (3) The chairman and members of the provincial government should comply with the Central Government's resolution and not be concurrently held by active military personnel. (4) The selection of personnel for each department should be limited to those with specialized knowledge and experience in the respective department. (5) The chairman of the provincial government should not concurrently hold or remotely lead other positions. (6) Provincial committee members who do not hold department positions should be required to take turns going out on inspection tours and accepting petitions and proposals from the people and be responsible for handling them. (7) The chairman of the provincial government should not remain in seclusion but should go out to inspect various counties in stages to examine the administration and have opportunities to get close to the people. (8) The provincial government and its departments should implement austerity policies, cut redundant staff and affiliated agencies (such as the Provincial Security Office and various bureaus affiliated with the departments). (9) Local autonomy should be implemented within a limited time frame in accordance with the Central Government's order. (10) Attention should be paid to developing the social economy and seeking relief for unemployed people. We earnestly request that the above points be considered and adopted to meet the earnest expectations of the 30 million people of Fujian. This urgent telegram expresses our deepest hopes. The United Association of Fujian Native Organizations in Shanghai kowtows.

Factory Association Opposes Compulsory Arbitration 173

Requests Assistance from the Bar Association

The Shanghai Machine-Made National Goods Factory United Association sent a letter to the Shanghai Bar Association yesterday, stating: We are writing to inform you that Mayor Wu of Shanghai proposed to the Central Political Conference that the Law on Handling Labor-Management Disputes be revised to restore compulsory arbitration. The 319th meeting resolved to submit the case to the Legislative Yuan for review. Since the Shanghai War, labor-management disputes have sprung up like mushrooms. Although there are many reasons for this, the legal system is certainly not unrelated. Since the Law on Handling Labor-Management Disputes was amended, labor-management disputes in Shanghai have been decreasing day by day, which is clear evidence. Under the current serious situation, foreign goods are being dumped at an increasing rate, and domestic goods are as stagnant as ever. Both labor and management are suffering greatly. How should they work together in the same boat to seek improvement? Unfortunately, labor strikes are occurring frequently, and disputes cannot be resolved. Their efforts are no different than hastening their own demise, which is regrettable. The government has complete laws and regulations for handling disputes, and if the law can be enforced, there is no way to resolve them. There seems to be no need to blame the legal system. Moreover, the current voluntary arbitration system allows for objections to arbitration and appeals to the court to correct human governance by law. The intention is excellent and fits the national situation. If it is changed to compulsory arbitration, there will be no way to appeal if the arbitration is improper. Not only will it violate the spirit of the rule of law, but also the consequences will be dire. Our association feels threatened and cannot remain silent. We have already presented our reasons to the Central Political Committee, the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, and the Ministry of Industry to strive to maintain the status quo and avoid increasing disputes. We have long admired your association's enthusiasm for maintaining industry and your thorough understanding of legal principles. We are sending you the original submission and copies of newspaper clippings, hoping that you will investigate and provide strong support. We ask you to raise your voice and be admired by all. The national economy and the people's livelihood rely on it. Respectfully, the Shanghai Machine-Made National Goods Factory United Association to the Shanghai Bar Association.

City Government Issues Ruling on Sanyou Factory Dispute 174

Regarding the shutdown dispute at the Sanyou Industrial Society's main factory in Yinxiang Port, the city government organized an arbitration committee, which formally submitted the case for arbitration the day before yesterday. The original text of the officially announced ruling is as follows:

Shanghai Labor-Management Arbitration Committee Ruling No. 20. Disputing Parties: (Labor) Shanghai Seventh District Cotton Weaving Industry Labor Union; (Management) Sanyou Industrial Society Co., Ltd. The aforementioned parties have a dispute arising from the closure of the Yinxiang Port Main Factory. Mediation by the mediation committee failed, and arbitration was requested. This committee shall handle it according to the law and rules as follows:

▲ Ruling: The Sanyou Industrial Society's Yinxiang Port factory shall restore a portion of its operations within three months, accommodating at least one-fifth of its original workforce. Before the resumption, the company shall provide workers with food allowances in proportion to their original wages. The remaining workers may be dismissed according to the original agreement, but when the Shanghai and Hangzhou factories hire workers, the dismissed workers shall be given priority employment.

▲ Facts: The Sanyou Industrial Society's Yinxiang factory, due to the sudden changes in Shanghai, was in a dangerous situation, and was forced to announce a complete cessation of work in all departments on January 29th of this year. Subsequently, the unemployed factory workers immediately demanded relief from the factory. After the ceasefire agreement, the workers demanded resumption of work. Management refused, citing excessive inventory, tight capital turnover, costs exceeding sales prices, and losses from the Shanghai Incident. Labor argued that the factory had substantial profits in previous years and recently established a large-scale Hangzhou branch, proving the development of the Yinxiang factory. Management's desire to close the original main factory disregards the past contributions of the workers, which is unreasonable. Workers, due to livelihood concerns, insisted on resuming work. Finally, the mediation committee proposed two options: (1) Restore a portion of operations, with the scale measured by the number of workers, a maximum of one-third and a minimum of one-fifth; (2) Dismiss the remaining workers, and prioritize hiring the old workers when hiring new workers in the future. Labor had already expressed its intention to accept, but management strongly rejected the partial resumption of work and requested arbitration. Meanwhile, the city government had decided that the management should provide labor with a daily food allowance of 120 silver dollars before the dispute was resolved. More than 20 workers, dissatisfied with the outcome, went on a hunger strike, expressing a final struggle. The dispute, which had been delayed for several months, became increasingly serious. Mediation failed. After the case was submitted to arbitration, this committee notified that a public arbitration would be held on August 31st. Due to some misunderstanding, the management did not attend, which is regrettable. However, arbitration is a public judgment, and summoning the parties is for consultation. The social bureau's mediation files show that the management representatives have repeatedly expressed their opinions, and the company's assets and liabilities have been thoroughly investigated and reported by accountant Xu Yongzuo. As this was not trusted by labor, the social bureau designated accountant Pan Xulun to conduct a re-examination, which is on file. Therefore, there is no need to notify the management to attend the meeting for debate or inquiry. A ruling should be made immediately.

▲ Reasons: According to the results of the audit by accountant Pan of Sanyou Industrial Society Co., Ltd., in the most recent three years, excluding annual depreciation, the surplus was over 132,000 yuan in the 18th year, over 218,000 yuan in the 19th year, and over 162,000 yuan in the 20th year. As of June 20th of this year, there was a loss of over 394,000 yuan. If the accumulated surplus from previous years and the public reserve fund, totaling over 195,000 yuan, are used to offset it, the actual loss is still less than 200,000 yuan. The depletion of the capital is only slightly less than 10%. Furthermore, the comparison of assets and liabilities of the company in the first half of this year was unsatisfactory to accountant Pan, who made a cautionary criticism. However, this comparison was similar in the 18th and 19th years, not just in the first half of this year, as evidenced by the asset and liability comparison table prepared by accountant Pan for the most recent three and a half years. Even if the Shanghai Incident losses are included, they are insufficient to justify closing the factory. Moreover, the issuing department is operating as usual, and the Hangzhou branch has not been suspended. It is inappropriate to close the oldest main factory with outstanding labor achievements. However, the company's losses in the first half of this year are almost equal to the total profits of the past three years, and its business prospects are indeed dangerous. Therefore, this committee believes that the final mediation proposal is appropriate, considering both labor and management, and should be adopted. Management should strive to restore one-fifth of the work within three months. The workers who cannot be accommodated should be dismissed according to the original agreement between labor and management, so that workers can seek alternative livelihoods. If the Yinxiang factory or the Hangzhou factory hire workers in the future, the dismissed workers should be given priority employment. Before the resumption of work and official dismissal, food allowances should be paid according to the original proportion to show sympathy, which is also the obligation of the management. This case was unanimously agreed upon by all members of this committee, and a ruling is made as stated in the main text. September 1, 1932, Chairman Luo Panhui, Committee Members Lu Jingshi, Shu Rong, Yang Peng, Zhao Shusheng, Xu Jileng.

After the Shanghai South Public Bus Company announced its temporary shutdown, the labor-management dispute has been resolved through mediation by party and government agencies. The details are as follows:

National Goods Factories Association Requests Increased Tax on White Paper 179

The Shanghai National Goods Factories Association submitted a letter to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry yesterday, requesting an increase in the tax on white paper in order to protect national goods, saying that recently foreign paper prices have been falling sharply, deliberately dumping in order to overwhelm domestic products. If a remedy is not sought quickly, how can national goods be maintained? Paper comes in many varieties. The customs import tariff has always levied a light tax on plain yellow paper by quantity, charging nine jiao per dan of customs gold, equivalent to about 20 taels of tax silver per ton. The market price of yellow paper is 60 taels per ton, and the tax rate is above 30%. Various white paper grades are taxed ad valorem, at 12.5% of the value. Based on a market value of 160 taels per ton, the tax silver is 18 or 19 taels, and the tax rate is only 11% or 12%. This white paper is used for making cigarette boxes and snack toy boxes. Judging from the classification of taxable goods, it seems that it can be classified as a luxury item, and its tax rate should be higher than that of yellow paper. The Legislative Yuan recently proposed increasing taxes on luxury goods. If the white paper is also changed to a quantitative tax, its tax rate can be increased to at least 2.5 to 3.5 yuan of customs gold per dan. In this way, customs revenue can be increased, and national paper will not be overwhelmed.

Orphan Rescued 185

Escaping Disaster...Seeking Help, Receiving Rescue

On August 31, the China Child Welfare Association received an orphan sent by Mr. Zhou Rongfu, requesting relief. After asking the child, it was learned that his name was Cheng Zhixiang, 16 years old, from Anhui. His father died when he was one year old, and he depended on his aunt along with his mother. He lived at No. 7 Chenjia Lane, Caidian River Street, Hankou. Because the Communist Party was causing trouble in that area, he and his mother fled, but they became separated on the road. He knew that his uncle, Cheng Zihuang, lived at No. 7, 5th Lane, Wenji Lane, Tangshan Road, Shanghai. He found his way to Shanghai alone, but his uncle had already moved due to the Sino-Japanese War. He had been stranded in Shanghai for ten days without food. He met Mr. Zhou, who brought him to this place, etc. When asked if he had any relatives, he said that his aunt's son, Yao Shouqing, worked at the Mobil Oil Company in Hankou, but he did not know in which department. He also had a brother-in-law named Cui Huisheng, who worked in the Yunmeng County Government in Hubei, but he did not know if he had moved. Because he had no travel expenses, he did not dare to go there rashly. The association only accepts orphans up to the age of twelve. The child was already sixteen, which did not meet the regulations. However, seeing that his situation was pitiable, he was temporarily sent to the Shanghai Child Welfare Education Institute, which is run by the association. A letter was sent to the child's relatives, and a notice was placed in the newspaper to help find them, in order to reunite the family.

Zhou Zhiqin Commits Suicide by Poisoning 191

Zhou Zhiqin, also known as Ruisheng, 25 years old, from Ningbo, who runs a sock business, checked into Room 37 of the Dongxinqiaokou No. 327 Huashang Hotel on Aiduya Road in the French Concession on the 28th of last month. For unknown reasons, he had a sudden impulse and committed suicide by taking poison. The next morning, the tea room attendant discovered him and sent him to Renji Hospital. Due to the deep poisoning, the treatment was ineffective, and he died at 1:30 AM yesterday. The hospital notified the police station, who transported the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home for examination. At 10 AM, Prosecutor Deng Baosun from the Second Special Court and a forensic doctor went to the funeral home to confirm that the deceased had died by taking poison. According to the tea room attendant Li Ayou, a woman came to visit the deceased before he died. He is currently trying to find the family of the deceased to collect the body. The official instructed that the body be temporarily kept at the police station pending collection by the family.

Post Office Receives European Mail 193

According to Shanghai Post Office news, on August 30, 20 bags of European mail shipped from Gange* via the Suez Canal were received. The bags contained mail from Munchen, Ansterdam, etc. Mail from London, Paris, and Berlin was not included. 164 bags of mail shipped from Japan via the Asama Marn were also received. The bags contained mail from London dated August 8 and 10, and mail from Berlin dated August 9 to 11. However, there was no mail from Paris. It is said that this is the first time that Siberian mail passing through Japan has been received. On the morning of August 31, 65 bags of Siberian mail transported by the Nanjing train were received. The names and dates of the sending offices are as follows: London, July 19-21 and July 26-28 (July 22-25 and July 29-August 7 not arrived); Paris, July 26-28 (July 22-25 not arrived); Berlin, July 20 and July 22 and July 27-29 (July 23-26 and July 30-August 8 not arrived).

Yu Shouzheng and Others' Self-Complaint Regarding Shi Zian and Others' Appeal 195

A Masterpiece by Lawyer Zhang Shizhao

Shi Zian, general manager of Yuansheng Securities Firm, colluded with Tian Hongnian, former manager of Zhonghui Bank, in acts of breach of trust and embezzlement, resulting in losses amounting to over 240,000 yuan. At the end of last year, shareholders Yu Shouzheng, Luo Kunxiang, and others pursued the matter in the first trial. The court ruled that the crime of breach of trust was established, but each defendant was only fined 1,000 yuan. The plaintiffs, dissatisfied, filed an appeal, represented by lawyers Zhang Shizhao, Dong Kang, and Peng Yuanxun. A few days ago, Judge Yu pronounced judgment, overturning the sentencing portion of the original verdict. Shi Zian was sentenced to one year of imprisonment for continuous breach of trust, along with a fine of 500 yuan. Tian Hongnian was sentenced to six months of imprisonment for joint breach of trust, along with a fine of 300 yuan. If the fines were not paid, they would be converted to imprisonment at a rate of three yuan per day. This information was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Lawyer Zhang Shizhao's appeal was widely praised. The following is an excerpt:

Yu Shouzheng and Others' Appeal Regarding Shi Zian and Tian Hongnian's Breach of Trust and Embezzlement, Filed in Their Own Name; Agent Lawyer Zhang Shizhao, Considering the Original Sentencing Too Lenient, Humbly Submits Additional Grounds for Appeal According to Law, Hoping to Change the Punitive Portion of the Original Judgment, to Uphold the Force of the Law and Punish Treacherous Merchants. Your humble servant, etc., are filing a self-complaint regarding the case of Shi Zian and Tian Hongnian, who colluded in breach of trust and embezzlement. On June 22 of this year, the Criminal Division of the First Special District District Court rendered a judgment (Case No. 395, Zhuang Di Zi, Year 20), the main text of which stated: "Shi Zian and Tian Hongnian are jointly guilty of breach of trust and are each fined 1,000 yuan. If the fines are not paid, they will be converted to imprisonment at a rate of three yuan per day," etc. It is evident that the original trial judge held a compassionate and merciful attitude, intending to use punishment to educate and deter. Your humble servant, etc., dare not disobey. However, Shi Zian and others are cunning and treacherous individuals, burdened with ill-gotten gains. Their lifelong habit is to recklessly squander the hard-earned money of others for their own illicit profits. The paltry sum of 1,000 yuan is, in their eyes, no more than a drop in the ocean. Punishment only restrains the honorable, while cunning is the forte of the petty. If one begins with a threatening appearance of harsh punishment but ends with a penalty that causes no pain or concern, it is like an arrow that misses the mark, amusing the monkeys. Ill-gotten gains are easily spent. The prohibition of wickedness will only nurture treachery, and the education of the capable will not correct violence. The state's goal of stopping crime and clarifying the law will not only be unattainable but will also have the opposite effect. The eyes of treacherous and deceitful individuals will be bolder and less discerning than ever. The facts are as such, and we dare not use alarming words to sensationalize. Several days after the pronouncement of the verdict, we heard that Shi Zian had gathered his business acquaintances and held a grand banquet to celebrate his victory in the lawsuit. Consider this: even though the penalty was established and his name was recorded in the penal register, he still called it a victory. What level of ignorance, shamelessness, and disregard for the law is this? One can easily infer more from this. The original judgment stated that if the fine was not paid, it would be converted to imprisonment. For those who have accumulated wealth through years of greed and spend money lavishly, using money to redeem their sentence is no different from giving away a hair. It goes without saying that the judgment is merely something for petty people to laugh and rejoice about. The state's use of punishment is originally intended to deter treachery, but it has ended up being manipulated and tested by treacherous individuals. How can one not lament this? Although your humble servants only pursue small profits, we know the boundaries of propriety. The loss of private property is a small matter, but the failure of the national law is a great matter. Fearing this, we dare not remain silent. Therefore, after receiving the original judgment, we declared an appeal to the original trial court within the statutory period and respectfully requested that the case file be sent for review, so that the presiding judge could begin the retrial. Now, in this supplementary statement of grounds, it seems that we should overturn and restate everything to ensure that nothing is omitted. However, in truth, we only seek to have the sentencing reconsidered and changed. As for the facts and reasons stated in the original judgment, after careful examination and verification, they are indeed accurate and flawless. Your humble servants, after reading them carefully, are filled with admiration. Since our knowledge is limited, there is no need for further elaboration. Examining the legal articles cited in the original judgment, there is indeed a range of possible sentences, and the fine can be imposed either separately or in conjunction with imprisonment. For example, Article 366 allows for imprisonment of up to five years, detention, and a fine. Furthermore, our country's code of criminal procedure is based on free evaluation, leading to a wide range of possible punishments for the same crime. The punishment that the offender should receive is determined by the judge's discretion at the time. The intention behind this is, on the one hand, similar to the principle of the Three Dynasties, where punishment was determined based on the specific circumstances (as stated in Zuo Zhuan, meaning that punishment was determined based on the situation, not by fixed laws). On the other hand, it contradicts the Legalist principle of aligning names with reality and adhering to legal formulas (as stated in the Lüshi Chunqiu). The benefits are widespread, but the harms are also associated with it. Why? Shi Zian and others have committed a crime under Article 366. Now, if they are told that they will be fined 1,000 gold, this is the same as telling them that they have committed the same crime. However, if they are told that they will be imprisoned for five years, the psychological impact on Shi and the effect on their behavior over the course of a year will be vastly different. Even a five-year-old child can understand this. Shi and others commit crimes entirely because they rely on their personal freedom to escape the law. The method of punishment should be based on the Zhouli, which places the person within a walled area and assigns them duties, which is sufficient to generate remorse and fear. As for money, it is precisely what they have hoarded in their chests. It is something easily obtained and difficult to exhaust. Whether it is Shi Zian or Tian Hongnian, who claims to have lost 240,000 yuan, who knows how much they really have hidden away? If the punishment is that they can be free of guilt by paying 1,000 yuan, then the wealth that Shi and Tian have cleverly seized from the public is precisely of this nature. If they can take one from a million and call it a punishment, then where would Shi and Tian not want to commit this crime? To reiterate, the 240,000 yuan they stole from others is now being nominally offset by 1,000 yuan, which is practically equivalent to being innocent. How many thousands of yuan do Shi and Tian have stored away to meet the need for such fines? Every time they spend 1,000 yuan, they can obtain 240,000 yuan. If these individuals continue to commit crimes again and again, will there ever be an end? The critics say that it is the court that encourages this. What will the officers of the law say? Furthermore, when your humble servants initiated the lawsuit in the original trial court, we consistently requested that the defendants be punished under Article 377 of the Criminal Law (see the first complaint and Lawyer Zhang's explanation of the defendant's crimes). The reason for this is that the crime of embezzlement committed by the defendants is based on a specific right, that is, according to law, contract, or care, etc., which falls under the so-called public or business duties mentioned in the law. According to this article, in addition to the increased term of imprisonment (seven years or less, six months or more), the fine can only be imposed in conjunction with imprisonment and cannot be converted to imprisonment. Now, although the original judgment listed the evidence of the crime in both the fact and reasoning sections, it was quite detailed, but the crime was only based on the article on breach of trust. The word "embezzlement" was not mentioned, and the origin of the business was difficult to determine. Shi Zian, as the general manager of Yuansheng Firm, has a very serious identity issue. All funds owned by the firm, whether capital, public reserve, deposits, or dividends, are all held by Shi Zian in his business capacity before they are legally distributed. The act of secretly depositing money into a private bank to evade responsibility is clearly a case of a custodian stealing from himself. It is a serious oversight to lightly treat it as continuous breach of trust. Even considering the breach of trust crime under Article 366, the sentence chosen in the original judgment is the lightest. Everything above that would have been more appropriate. According to Article 76 of the Criminal Law, when sentencing, all circumstances should be considered as the standard for determining the severity of the sentence within the statutory range. The so-called consideration of circumstances includes the causes, consequences, and intentions of the crime. Shi and Tian colluded as close relatives through their wives and abused their power to transfer funds from Zhonghui Bank for their own speculative purposes involving hundreds of thousands of yuan. The cause cannot be said to be small. Zhonghui Bank demanded repayment, and the appellants were unable to pay, resulting in the loss of their family assets and even endangering their lives. As for the current situation, the appellants have repaid Zhonghui Bank 150,000 yuan, and their other outstanding debts amount to no less than 100,000 yuan. The initial capital of 50,000 taels and the profits from previous years are not even being counted. The appellants have suffered greatly as a result, leading to the cessation of business. The consequences cannot be said to be insignificant. When the firm was in urgent need, Shi Zian claimed illness and fled, ignoring the firm's debts. When there were any deposits, he secretly transferred them to a bank that had no previous dealings with the firm. Even after the matter was exposed, he secretly instructed his partners to divide the remaining funds to avoid confiscation. In short, all the benefits went to him, and all the harms went to others. His intentions can be said to be extremely selfish. Comparing these serious matters with the principal punishment determined in the original judgment, it is clear that there is a serious imbalance. All of this has left your humble servants confused and helpless. We respectfully request a reconsideration. This is not a groundless complaint. Although business is declining and industries are withering, this is due to various reasons. However, merchants who do not abide by ethics and violate the law, treat all cases under the jurisdiction of the civil court as mere formalities and do not review them. They are skilled at stealing and hiding in multiple places. When managing a business, they do not invest in obvious assets, making it impossible to dispose of them and difficult to seize them. Those who follow the rules and perform their duties in the market are sacrificed and exploited. All of this is helpless. Such things are major problems that cannot be ignored. Therefore, the case involves more than just the private property of your humble servants. If we do not impose strict punishments and warn the world, people will stop working hard, and treacherous individuals will flourish. Since the opening of trade with foreign countries, Chinese merchants have been known for their honesty and integrity, but this old morality has gradually disappeared. When entering the world of commercial warfare, how far will the decline of Chinese commerce and the elimination of talent reach? Your humble servants cannot predict this. The presiding judge has keen insight and is determined to punish wrongdoing. Based on the above, although the scope of this case is small, its implications are broad. Who is to blame? Who caused this? Once clarified, it will be as clear as day. Without strict laws, how can diseases be cured? Without officials, how can diseases be treated? Your humble servants, fulfilling their duty as common citizens and thinking of the cries of the people, dare to request that this case be reconsidered, that the original judgment be overturned, and that the lenient sentencing be changed. If there is no leniency for crimes, there will be no trace of punishment. Then all punishments will be effective, and the law will not be a mere formality. The strong will be restrained, and the weak will be encouraged to do good. The atmosphere of the marketplace will be renewed, and the nation's vitality will be restored. Your humble servants pray for the country and the people even more than this. Respectfully submitted.

Maid Steals Master's Property During Shanghai War, Sentenced 196

A Cantonese woman named Zhong Wangshi, residing at 1099 North Sichuan Road, took refuge with relatives during the January 28th Shanghai War. She entrusted her clothes and jewelry, worth over 2,000 yuan, to her employed maid, Qin Yushi, for safekeeping. However, Qin Yushi, seeing the wealth, became greedy and colluded with Zhuang Shilin, Zhu Dasheng, and others from Pudong to steal the clothes and jewelry and flee. After the case was reported, detective Sun Aizhong arrested Qin Yushi and the other three, including Zhuang Shilin's wife, Wan, and recovered a portion of the stolen goods. They were handed over to the First Special District Court. After repeated hearings, the court concluded the case yesterday morning and announced the judgment. Judge Shen Bingrong, presiding over the criminal court, sentenced Qin Yushi, Zhuang Shilin, Zhu Dasheng, and Zhuang Wan to one year of imprisonment each. The number of days of pre-trial detention will be deducted from their sentences. The stolen goods were returned to the plaintiff, Zhong Wangshi, after she signed a receipt.

Letter to the Editor 210

To the Editor:

We have reviewed yesterday's newspaper report of [Shanghai South Public Bus Company after ceased operation yesterday issued unpaid salaries]. It does not align with the facts. As for the issue of unpaid wages, representatives from the Party and government authorities announced on August 30 that they would be paid at 3:00 PM on August 31. However, the company authorities repeatedly delayed the payment. All the workers waited at the company until 8:00 or 9:00 PM, but the unpaid wages were still not paid. There was no police presence to maintain order. This type of news that distorts the facts is likely to cause confusion. Please correct it immediately.

Sincerely,

Shanghai South Public Bus Company Union
